when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她的確做過一些 , 但真正的事情是 , 真正的意義是 , 未來會比這更多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈在1936年重複發明電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是純機械的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論性的
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都來自數學的觀點 , 但turing告訴我們一些很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他奠定了數學在電腦科學上的基礎 , 說: 「 你怎麼把電腦創造出來的並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣是純機械的 , 或是像今天這種電子的 , 都不重要也許未來的電腦是細胞 , 或是再一次的 , 同樣的 , 機械方面 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 ,
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 這些東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 計算的本質
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做church-turing論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你會看到這個連結 , 說babbage當年造的 , 真的是一部電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到所有我們現今用電腦做的 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓大家了解有多慢 , 有一個大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 輸入卡 , 並且它的速度比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一個ram背包
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要 , 你可以增加很多額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 我們今天在哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典科學博物館的檔案有上百個計劃和上千頁文獻是charlesbabbage寫的、關於這個分析引擎的筆記
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一系列計畫被我們稱作計劃28這也是我與doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字他是科學博物館的計算機部門也就是開車這個計劃要建造出一個不一樣引擎的人我們的計劃就是把它做出來
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有許多部分可以做 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經做過的 。 第二個是研究所有計劃的成果 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部份是一個模擬那機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部份是實際在博物館中製造 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你將終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前的不是一片極小的晶片 , 而是要看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作、cpu在運作、我聽見它運作的聲響 。 我說不定還聞的到 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們會做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫到 , 一旦分析引擎真的被製造出來它一定會對未來的科學有所幫助
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有把它做出來 , 因為他總是在瑣碎新的計劃 , 但是當它真的在1940年代被建造出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我先讓各位稍微了解一下它的動作狀況 , 影片中只顯示cpu運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這是三組齒輪它準備做加法 。 這是加法的運作原理所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們會擁有
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場受歡迎的演說中 , 雅恩•亞伯特蘭展示了他最近的三大項目 , 內容是關於人性以及我們的棲息地 , 在他的一系列 「 從地球出發 」 中 , 個人的訪談 , 透過他的網路專案 「 六十億人 」 展現了他的近期作品 , 內容是關於人類的電影 , 透過拍攝視頻 , 記錄了人類對於環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarhusbertrand從廣角度捕捉到脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球造成很大的影響 , 可以搭乘飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	在大氣中 , 我排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裏是為了談談生態問題 , 我一年內排放的二氧化碳量相當於一個法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我得做什麼呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵銷碳 , 就像我每次做這件事 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是要呈現出我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我在去年所拍攝的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油砂 , 很多污染

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們一天24小時不停地工作 , 74小時後 , 以便儘可能提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油終結 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油沙不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油總量是每年所發現的三倍 。

coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞州的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年之前 , 珊瑚有100%可能會因為全球暖化而被消滅 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的無障礙演說中 , 理查德•瑞斯尼克說明了經費和快速基因組定序是如何將健康照護顛倒過來 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命運動
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我為大家介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女生有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男生有x染色體 , 當然還有那一小段y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	<unk>男孩們<unk>只是一個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 會看到雙螺旋結構生命的編碼是由四個生化字母組成 , 我們稱之為基對 , 是a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組有多少基對呢 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	每個人都可以隨便丟出一堆很大的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但實際上 , 如果我把這1280像素高800像素高80像素的每一個像素放在一起 , 我們就需要3000塊螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為有一群人 , 順便一提 , 有y染色體的人決定想要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以事實上 , 15年後 , 花了約40億美金後 , 基因組就被定序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最終的版本發表 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每根鹼基的成本大約是一美元這是非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們將一個基因組複製50份然後將這些複製品分割成50基對接著我們將它們排序 , 大量平行
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶入軟體中 , 把它重新組合 , 告訴大家故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓你們對圖片更瞭解 , 人類基因組計劃:3gb , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	每週可以做2000億基對 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	而今年夏天 , 600位將會改變 , 沒有一點 「 緩慢 」 的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 要以一個鹼基排序定序的代價 , 已經下跌一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就相當於你在1998年給汽車加滿一次油的錢 , 一直等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星又來了兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 電腦普及 , 醫學文獻的存檔 , 摩爾定律 , 舊的定序方法 , 而這一新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數刻度 , 你通常不會看到像那樣上升的線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以全世界用於人類基因組測序的能力可以在今年做到5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	根據被放置的機器 , 我們知道這點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	在可預見的未來裏每年這個數字都會翻倍 , 或三倍甚至四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間實驗室佔據了所有容量的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國絕對是贏得此次比賽的新月球順便一提
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人年紀是37歲
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現了階段2的雌激素受阻體陽性乳腺癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術 , 化療和放射性治療
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又發現了第三個卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲又回來了卵巢癌更是化療
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道衰竭 , 8天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 小至10年 , 這位女士接受治療的方式 , 將會看起來如同放血一般 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因研究所的同事rickwilson決定要看一下這位女士的來信
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他依序排序 , 他找了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 以及抗癌的骨髓 , 在幾週內就完成了兩者的基因組定序 , 沒有大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他在軟體中比對這兩組基因 , 然後他發現 , 在一個稱為tp53的基因上 , 一個二千個鹼基的消息在一個叫做tp53的基因裡 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因上有這種惡意的突變基因 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女性沒有幫助 , 但這對她的家人卻有嚴重、深遠的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我是說 , 如果他們有相同的突變基因檢測 , 並且獲得相同的基因檢測 , 然後他們能去做定期的檢測 , 就可以及早發現癌症 , 而且有可能更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我來介紹beery雙胞胎在兩歲時被診斷出大腦性麻痺
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信這些症狀並不搭配 , 透過一些英勇的努力 , 和許多網際網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服這個醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的力量 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的就是肌張力不足的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 症狀的確有所改善 , 但並不完全是症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	幸運的是照片中的這位先生叫做joebeery , 他在一家叫做生命科技的公司擔任首席事務總裁 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造這些巨大全基因組測序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是為他的孩子做基因測序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現了一系列稱為spr的基因突變 , 其中負責製造血清素 , 和其他的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給這些孩子使用血清素前發性藥物 , 現在他們非常正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有全基因組測序是不可能發生的 。

so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	像蝙蝠俠和水槍一樣小

and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃飯時 , 他的腸道基本上會打開排泄物溢出到他的腸子 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	於是數百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 拜託幫我禱告 。 我現在很痛苦 。 」

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫特展示了他的骨髓礦工一個新裝置 , 很快就能收集拯救生命的骨髓 , 帶給捐贈者最少的痛苦 。 他強調在骨髓中所發現的成體幹細胞可以被用來治療許多臨終的疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術房 , 還有bob , bob是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們要把他的骨髓發送到全國 , 拯救患有白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個完整的o.r.團隊 , 麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一個醫生在我面前
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們將這一小根針 , 你知道 , 不要太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是把這個針筒放在軟組織裡 , 每一次用針筒將它打入硬骨頭 , 插入tuchus 。 用針筒來約十毫升的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把針筒傳給護士 , 她把針筒收起來
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	再將它傳回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三的重複這樣的行為 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到最後 , 我的手臂酸痛 , 我手上接到一通電話 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股 , 看起來就像這個 , 像個瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	因此我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序四十年來並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	應該可以有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了用微創的方法 , 和一種我們稱為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新儀器 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而 「 骨髓採取器 」 , 它的運作方式是以
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準來看待病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	相對於進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入髖骨的前面 , 或後面的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個有彈性、發電的導管 , 內部有一個特別的電線圈 , 它保持在骨髓的脆弱部分 , 當它移動時 , 會跟著臀部的輪廓 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	它讓你快速渴望或吸出豐富的骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以透過同一個入口多次進出 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	因此 , 非常迅速地 , bob只需一個穿刺當地麻醉的功能即可拿來做為門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小額資助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再來玩一下
and our team members developed this technology .	我們團隊的成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們又拿到兩隻大型動物 , 以及豬研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令人驚訝的是 , 我們不僅取出了骨髓 , 還從骨髓採取的骨髓細胞活動量是從骨髓採取器取得的十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置去年剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一位活病人 。 你可以在有彈性的曲線附近看到 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人 , 同一個病人 , 同一個病人 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉、門診、
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 比起在同一個病人身上 , 製造標準療法 , 我們得到了大約三到六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	各位都知道胚胎幹細胞 ,
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	它們潛力無窮 , 但還未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包括在骨髓內的血液幹細胞 , 這種幹細胞療法我們已經使用了超過四十年的幹細胞療法 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年 , 有爆炸性的骨髓幹細胞 , 用來治療病患其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、骨關節炎、組織工程 , 甚至是用神經系統來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛公佈 , 正在商業化今年2.0世代的骨髓採取器 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望可以取出更多幹細胞 , 翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在更年輕、更健康的將來 , 儲存你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 以備你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者加雷特•賴西提出了一個很有爭議的宇宙模型 , 這個模型可能可以解答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它就是最美麗的八度空間模型 , 代表基本粒子和力量 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、技術、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	嘉瑞特.萊西的理論是有關萬物的理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看這些殺手級方程式吧 , 真可愛 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的十八分鐘我會盡力在不用方程式的描述粒子物理的美好之處
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且非比尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一隻珊瑚的頭都由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地繁殖和分枝 , 成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這會是高智商的珊瑚我們會想出一個人問他一個合理的問題
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他到底是怎麼走到這一特定的地點 , 和他的鄰居相比 , 如果是剛好是命運 , 還是怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們收到溫度升高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚有一定的意義 , 你看 , 我衝浪的傷疤可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這一罐珊瑚會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居就是非常一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他地方也是 。 但是作為一個獨立的個體 , 體驗他
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 高智商的珊瑚可以特別準備來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實世界和珊瑚一樣也具有不同的可能性 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	我們人類很難理解這種思維 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異性最早是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這組裝中 , 薛丁格處在一個具有放射性樣本的盒子中 , 根據量子力學定律 , 將這些樣本分成一個放射性、一個不受輻射照射的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	樣本盛行的分支造成了觸發因子釋放毒氣薛丁格必死無疑
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在另一個分支的現實裡 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都能分別感受到這些現實
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	就某一方面來說 , 另一種不能
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們看不到其他分支的存在 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每個人 , 和薛丁格一樣 , 是一種珊瑚分支 , 分支延伸到不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以做
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學剩下的就是去描述哪些可以發生 , 哪些不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可用幾何學加上基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下事情才有可能發生
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將講說明我們對這些粒子的認識它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反質子會被加速到接近光速的速度 , 然後相撞 , 產生出一股單純能量爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這些能量立刻轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 與用來研究其特性的探測器和電腦 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器--在日內瓦的歐洲核子研究中心的大型強子對撞機周長有17英里運轉時對撞機的能量是蒙特雷市的五倍
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確預測在任何個體碰撞中 , 會有什麼樣的粒子 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有的可能性都已實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子可以被製造出來 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量都必須有質子和反質子的能量
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更大的粒子都不會產生 , 並且保持我們看不見的形態 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新型粒子加速器那麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越過去7倍的能量極限 , 因此我們很快會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談論我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們多數人熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的很多人 , 過著很好的生活 , 把他們推到附近 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子有個中性的夥伴叫做中子不帶電且有著極小的質量
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下夸克有很大的質量 , 再把三個加在一起 , 就能做出原子裡面的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些粒子分為兩類左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代電量和第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和各種力量產生交互作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	帶電粒子通過光子傳遞電磁力相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很微弱的力 , 叫做微弱的力 , 只與左旋的物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克以色荷為載體通過強力相互作用色荷分三種紅綠藍
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪默里•蓋爾曼 , 這些名字都是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力 , 它的質量和物質相互作用 , 通過旋轉 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷和物質發生作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一種尚未見過但我們很確定存在的粒子是希格斯粒子它給予所有其他粒子的質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子我們確信它將會
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的奧秘在於我們還能看到什麼
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我會在演講最後向你們展示這美好的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算所有不同的粒子共有226種
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	要追蹤這些粒子的數量很多 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子是很奇怪的
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們按他們各自的載荷把他們畫出來 , 一些美麗的圖案就會浮現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子擁有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克合成一個質子它就擁有加1的總電荷
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 帶有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	電荷實際上是另兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這種模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	稱為電弱統一模型於1967年組裝
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力更加弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	既然大量的希格斯粒子在水平方向分佈在這張圖中 , 電磁力的光子仍然是沒有質量的 , 在載荷空間中和電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二維空間中通過粒子載荷的型式表示出來
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後把載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間以便我們能觀察到
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子如何作用自然會在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	粒子如果和它的反粒子相撞會產生能量四個電荷方向的載荷疊加變為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 並保持完全的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持一個完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們哪些互動是可以發生的
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 以便更好地看透強相互作用 , 這個互動有著不錯的六角形對稱體 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子比如說這個會和有色夸克相互作用比如這個綠夸克會給夸克帶來不同的色荷比如這個紅夸克
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每一個原子裏發生上百萬次把原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但是與三種力相對應的這四種載荷還不是終點
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以多納入兩個載荷相對應地心引力
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些加入後 , 每個粒子會有兩個不同的自旋載荷 , 自旋向上和自旋向下 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中形成了一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案符合我們目前對於大自然在微小尺度下建造出的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們能確定的
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中可以達到的極限
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道了細小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙與這些微小尺度運行的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但是現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的新和舊的想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看能不能把我們的手放在整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新粒子 , 何時實驗能達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷圖案 , 不太對稱 , 可以從更完美的圖案中發現 , 跟希格斯粒子破壞電弱圖案一樣 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目標 , 我們需要引入具有新的載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們要導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷 , 然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜測我們可以在六度載荷空間中建構標準載荷集作為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個選擇與1973年由帕蒂和薩拉姆推出的一個大統一理論相應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的合成圖案 , 我們可以看到一些空白區域 , 粒子似乎不見了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的研究方式
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家將已有的結構作為子集 , 尋找更大、更對稱的結構 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們得以預測那些從未見過的粒子的存在
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新的粒子它們應該和弱力很像 , 只是比較弱而已
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子通過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間上彼此相互坐著
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以對每一個粒子給予獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代通過一種叫 " 三重性 " 的對稱性與第一代物質有關聯
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最漂亮的幾何結構之一
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型謊言小組的模式 , e8
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案的每一點都能對應到這個複雜而美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的彎曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	再加上量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙是如何以最細微的尺度運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	八度載荷空間中這個形狀的圖案是顯而易見的它概括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種都只是這個複雜形狀的表面
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	轉動它時可以看到包含其中的許多錯綜複雜的圖案
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過某種旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何一種放大法則 , 我們可以看到在這個圖案中 , 新粒子被需要的地方 ,
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	在這有20個空格需要新粒子其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子應該像希格斯粒子一樣稀少但具有色荷且和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	許多人認為它是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個了不起的前景這個擁有偉大數學美的物體可以用想像得到的最小尺度描述粒子相互作用的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的這個想法一點都不新 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年伽利略寫了這段話: 「 大自然的偉大著作 , 即停止對我們的凝視 , 被數學的語言所寫 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他的幾何形狀 , 在沒有這些的狀況下 , 是人性中不可能理解的單一個字 ; 如果沒有這些 , 又會在黑暗的迷宮中遊走 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述粒子物理的數學性
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家在研究這東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但可以確保數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學一起形成的數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用著一個美麗的圖案
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	當使用大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器時 , 我們可能可以知道到底e8圖案還是另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然也對我個人不利
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還不錯 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作是個非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的理論都是長期的結果 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部份這些想法可能最後都不是大自然的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有大量的擦殺事件 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司一樣
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同對任何大型投資 , 當它行不通時 , 都會很難拋棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得要把它丟掉 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡可能的過著一種平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我研究的物理學也沒想到 , 我還是過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	並試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在我父母最大的疑惑是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們知道這個秘密
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	各位可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象相似 , 但在稍微不同的位置 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種很不尋常的生活
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難 , 但卻讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 並保持我人生的平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚混在一起 ,
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很欣賞超級聰明人士的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請到ted來 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能聽懂了百分之二的部分 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 之所以能讓少數人感到興奮 , 是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 那就把重力和量子理論結合在一起了 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你是不是說我們應該認為宇宙是內心最小的東西 , 有可能就是e8物體嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我是說 , 有沒有一個最小的尺寸可以比喻為
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我展示給你們看的圖案跟我們所知的基本粒子物理而且這已經是非常美麗的圖案了
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	就是那個我說我們知道是肯定的
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	而這個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似之處與e8圖案的原理相似可能是其他的圖片
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點狀圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 在我們所經歷的空間中 , 會被扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有我們看到的基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 就我所理解的 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何想像在e8中和電子的關係呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不 , 它會是這個e8形狀對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以當這個形狀在時空中移動 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時它扭曲的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以--克:e8形狀的大小 , 電子的大小 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	大嗎 ? 小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:就我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這點會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都在同時展開發展
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是我為什麼用它來對珊瑚作類似的比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此 , e8的進入方式便是成為一個連接時空中每一點的形狀
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲方向是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以在量子場理論中 , 它們會以這些點來呈現它們自己 , 並且以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能解釋得更清楚 ,
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了一種奇蹟 , 而我肯定想了解的更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但是非常謝謝你來 。 真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍.古德爾談到坦尚尼亞還有其它的社區計畫 , 這些計畫幫助非洲城鎮的人並肩生活在受到威脅的動物之間 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球性議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以這樣說 , 辦得到 , 坐擁好了 , 但是我們也可以ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , oooh , ooh
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩的叫聲在晚上他們要去睡覺前
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的這一端傳到另一端 , 從這一群巢穴傳到下一處 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今晚我想從昨天拉斯離開的地方來聽我的演說 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的三歲澳洲小孩塞蘭姆
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過透過dna的基因檔案 , 關於人類的歷史、族譜
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一名古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯利基 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩之路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在那個時代 , 實在是相當不凡 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在則已廣為人知 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	從化石你可以知道很多生物長什麼樣子從肌肉的形狀、肌肉連接所得的形狀 , 關於牠們從各式各樣的人造物身上過生活的方式 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但是他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然行為不是化石
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張──而且現在是個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在現存最接近的遠親--人猿 , 和現今的人類祖先中發現行為模式相似或相同 , 那麼 , 也許那些行為在七百萬年前就出現了 , 人類的祖先中也出現了 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把那些特質從那個古老的往事中帶過一遍 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你去看現今要處理人類進化的教科書 , 你經常會看到人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比任何其他生物更像我們 。 在這個ted會議中 , 我們已經聽過了 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這仍然是我要評論的黑猩猩在某些方面是如此地與我們相似
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有牠或牠自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到六十歲或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部份的牠們應該不會在野外生存到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	溫柔先生 , 母蚊子在11至12歲時生了第一個小孩 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她每五到六年就只有一名嬰兒 , 那是一段長時間的孩童依賴期 , 那時的孩童能哺育、晚上和母親睡覺 , 然後騎在她的背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的孩童依賴期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們來說 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在生物不同的演化過程中變得更為複雜所以我們發現在個體的生命史中 , 學習扮演著越來越重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 正是這種方式 , 如今在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中所研究的不同的使用工具行為模式 , 這些行為如何從一個世代的傳給下一代 , 通過觀察、模仿和練習 , 如此一來 , 我們就可以把這些使用工具的行為描述成是原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口說的語言 。 我們剛剛已經談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們確實有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多都和我們的一模一樣 , 且用同樣的情境來形式形成 。 迎接黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍另一個人的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們大搖大擺地往下扔 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現了很多很多的例子 , 關於同情心、愛的前兆 , 以及真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 就像我們人類一樣 , 牠們也有天生的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們具有極端殘暴的能力 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常激進的行為 , 大多數的情況下 , 都會被引導出去對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們有非常強烈的地域性
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們更加了解 , 畢竟人類和動物王國之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條界線其實非常的模糊 , 而且在我們做出更多的觀察之後它變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍在持續 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會關係中的黑猩猩們 , 幫助我們遠遠超過其他任何事情 , 讓我們意識到我們也是其中的一份子 , 而不是與我們同享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 跟世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都很感傷 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張由空中拍攝的照片 , 它呈現了岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那是我十六年前飛越整片地區時 , 那時我意識到 , 在公園之外 , 在公園之外 , 這個森林有 , 1960年時 , 沿著坦岡易科湖東邊的海岸 , 那個地方很小 , 30平方英呎的岡貝國家公園所在之處 , 有一個問題就在我腦海裡出現 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	" 我們該如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩們 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人民正為了生存而苦苦掙扎時 ? "
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	住在這裡的人數超過了可能會支持土地 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	持續增加的難民們如洪水般從蒲隆地湧入以及剛果的湖面上方 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人們買不起他們在別處購買的食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱它為坦尚尼亞造林計劃 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面性的改善在公園附近村莊的人們的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	開始的計畫是小規模的 , 有12個村莊 。 現在它已經24個村莊了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間詳細說明 , 但它包含了諸如樹林哺乳類、養殖最適合這種方式的農業 , 如同在這些山區過度分解 , 幾乎是像沙漠般的土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤流失的方法
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 讓農地在兩年內可以再度生產 ,
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民們從井裡能取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些校間
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信是和一小群婦女合作提供她們取得微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們已經有 , 就如同全世界的情況一樣 , 大約95%的貸款都退還了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	給予女性權力 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 這樣她們才能完成中學學教育 , 可以清楚了解到 , 隨著女性教育的增長 , 全世界的家庭人數減少 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭計劃與愛滋病等資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 有些事發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	對於保育這24個村莊的農夫們 , 不要把我們當成一群白種人來研究一群猴子 , 順便說一句 , 很多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 那是一個坦尚尼亞人進入村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康感興趣 , 對教育感興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解山坡地的上層結構是用樹木來做計算的 , 所以你有了這種可怕的土壤侵蝕和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在開發更大的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠超出國家公園 , 延伸到所有這些十分貧瘠的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準的時候 , 他們其實也同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地保留下來 , 所以再一次的 , 當樹木長回來之後 , 黑猩猩們將會有一道樹葉路過 , 藉此 , 牠們可以與國家公園外的其他遺傳群體進行互動 。
so tacare is a success .	坦尚尼亞造林計劃是一大成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們就把它複製到非洲的其它區域 , 其它荒野面臨極端人口壓力的區域 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 正如我們前面這幾天一直在討論的問題 , 都是很重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有著大量的貧窮
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量人居住在沒有那麼肥沃的土地上 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 讓土壤開放給腐化的土壤 , 當絕望的人口砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 如此他們就能嘗試種植食物給自己和家人 , 接下來會發生什麼事 ? 一定得要付出代價 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不只在非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家還有 , 無所不在地我們對我們的星球做了些什麼呢 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人都達到了生活水準 , 那我們需要三個新的地球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現在 , 他們說四個 。 但是我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們現在可以說是地球上最聰明的生物 , 帶有非凡的頭腦 , 能運用這麼好看的科技 , 從這些ted研討會中看出端倪 , 但我們卻破壞了唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民在作出重大決定之前 , 曾坐在一旁問自己: 「 這個決定是如何影響我們未來的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我在這裡談的不是非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 還有數百萬人 , 通常都是以 「 這會如何影響下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決策對非洲的影響
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行時 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 與他們消失的森林 , 我了解到越來越多非洲的問題 , 可以在以前殖民時代被利用 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	不論在哪裡 , 都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你懂我在說什麼 。 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣經常會毒害我們 ,
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是其中一個對我們這世紀來說所要面對的最關鍵的課題 。 四周的水正在被污染著 , 被農業、工業、家中的化學品污染著 , 這些化學物質仍然被散播到全世界 , 看似無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 如海嘯所帶來的影響更加嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經說過土壤的流失問題 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不計後果的燃燒著石化燃料 , 和其他溫室氣體一起燃燒 , 所以說 , 造成氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人開始相信 , 我們的氣候是有狀況的 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候是混雜的 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是窮人受到更深的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	已經受影響的非洲 ,
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南的非洲地區乾旱更加嚴重
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來的時候 , 它很常導致洪水和苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓與疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在無法支援的土地上的人數 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 無法搬出去的人數 , 因為土地都退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	因而造成沙漠危害雖然最後一棵樹已經砍伐
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這樣的事並不只發生在非洲 。 在全世界都是如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我一點也不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可以有某種程度的落差存在於這個特別聰明的大腦 , 那種出現在ted科技上 , 再放大到人類心中的思維嗎 ? 用非科學的角度來說 , 談到愛和同情的話題 。 會不會有所不足之處嗎 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 或冷漠的 , 或痛苦和憤怒的 。 他們說的或多或少都說了同樣的話 , 「 我們會有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經損害了我們的未來 , 但我們卻束手無策 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經損害了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每一次我看著他們我想我們從我還是他們的時候 , 怎樣傷害了這個美麗的星球 , 我感受到他們的絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這個計畫我們稱之為根與芽 , 這個計畫從坦尚尼亞這裡開始 , 目前已經擴及全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它有象徵性的意義 。 根部建立堅固的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來很小 ; 為了要到達太陽 , 它們能穿過一堵磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆比作所有這些問題地球上所造成的所有的環境和社會問題 。 這是關於希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以突破這困境 , 為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	" 根與芽 " 計畫所傳達最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人每天都有所成就 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們是有選擇權的 。 每一個在這間會議室的人 , 我們都能選擇怎樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇這取決於我們要改變現狀 , 使得窮人也能選擇
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的小組都選了三個計劃 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論是在城市或鄉村 , 或什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從幼兒園到大學都有的方案 , 有越來越多的成人開始做他們自己的根與芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每一個小組都選擇三個不同的項目來讓這個世界更美好 , 並認識到這些不同的問題彼此之間都緊密相連 , 並且互相影響著 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們其中一個計畫將是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	再來 , 如果他們能做到 , 他們可能會募集資金 , 來協助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物們 , 不只是野生的動物們 , 還有那些家養的動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫是去幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這一切 , 都是一個信息:學習以和平與和諧的方式生活在我們自己、家庭、我們的社群、國家之間、文化與文化之間、宗教之間、和我們與自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能再以目前的速度繼續破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們擁有的不只是這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要看看一個或兩個在非洲的計畫 , 這些計畫的根與芽團體正在進行 , 一兩個計畫只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果 , 布拉崗 , 獅子山 , 喀麥隆和其他的團體們 。 正如我說的 , 目前涵蓋在全球97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 。 他們在種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 和雞一起工作 , 用賣的雞蛋得到一點點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽家人 , 讓他們感到自豪和自主 , 因為他們不再無助而且依賴別人用蔬菜和雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	在烏干達也在心理上幫助了一些之前是童兵的小孩們 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	進行這樣子的計畫能讓他們脫離自我
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的一份子 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄中也有這個專案 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間更多的根與芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要組成部份 , 讓年長的小孩和年紀較小的孩子說話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而非自願性的懷孕之類的年輕人會傾聽年輕人的心聲更好 , 而非成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 , 我在世界各地被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你看到了這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看到你的黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬隻的數量 , 在本世紀之交 , 到現在不超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的地方
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣沒有希望的大會 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是神奇的人腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想技術
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我實在太激動了 , 最終 , 來到人們面前談論堆肥式的公廁 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往馬桶裡沖 , 情況很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後談到再生能源極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否會為我們的孩子關心地球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否關心他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界上菁英的精英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出一些選擇 , 來作為我們每一天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這個問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	它會如何影響我孩子長大後的人生 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其他的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人類的大腦 , 與人的心結合 , 我們就牽著手環繞世界 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted能幫助我們的原因 , google也協助我們 , esri也幫我們繪製貢貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 它開始發生 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	這個下午你們已經聽過了 , 現在開始
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這個改變 , 這個改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們一定會有的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	另一個原因是希望自然是令人驚異的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以讓一塊完全被毀壞的區域 , 只要有時間或許再一些幫助 , 就能讓它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而坦尚尼亞造林計劃就是一個例子 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我說過 , 看似已死去的樹木殘根假如你停止砍伐他們來生火 , 你就不需要因為你已經擁有很多的木材了 , 那麼在五年之內 , 你就有一棵30英尺的樹了 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物們 , 幾乎就在絕種的邊緣 , 卻有第二次機會.這是我的下一本書.
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它啟發了我 。 它也帶領我看到了最後一種希望類型 。 在這過去兩天中 , 我們已經聽到了很多 。 這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人們堅決的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以那些你認為會被貧窮或疾病擊垮的人們 , 或其他什麼 , 可以讓他們自己挺身而出 , 有時只要一個幫手 , 讓他們成為社會的一分子 , 讓他們成為改變這個世界的一份子 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	試想一下 , 在非洲有一、兩位 , 都是非常鼓舞人心的人 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一份很長的清單 , 但顯然尼爾森•曼德拉從17年的辛苦勞工 , 23年的監禁中湧現出來 , 有很了不起的寬恕 , 所以他能夠帶領他的國家在沒有血腥對抗的情況下擺脫種族隔離的惡劣政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的沙羅維瓦對抗著巨大的石油公司 。 儘管全世界的人都竭盡心力 , 但卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是多麼的鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 就是我們在非洲年輕人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境榜樣 , 今天也聽過一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會再次與在ted的各位分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	在那個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書 , 十分興奮 。 她是根與芽的根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這能幫助她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常振奮人心 , 能夠見到她 , 並僅僅是一個例子 , 關於年輕人當他們被賦予能力 , 給予這個機會去行動 , 讓這個世界變得更好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些棘手的事實 , 關於塑膠污染在海洋裡、生活中 , 以及一些想法 , 說明如何將我們自己從塑膠垃圾回收中解放 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義 , 全球性議題 , 綠色 , 使命藍色 , 海洋 , 塑膠 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我同時也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	塑膠袋是我主要的創作材料我把這些塑膠袋剪開再縫合拼湊起來已經有20年了
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二度和三度空間 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	我和塑膠一共工作大約八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始產生裂變 , 分解成更小的塑膠碎片 。
and i thought , " great .	我想: 「 太好了 ,
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在更進一步的教育我自己時 , 其實我意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	把塑膠分解成小塊的壞東西 , 因為它永遠都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現在海洋環境裡 , 很多的
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應 , 我認為這是很多人第一次對學習這件事有所反應: 「 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須走出去把這東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的制定了一個計劃跟一艘貨船及兩艘退休的拖網漁船、一座起重機、一台磨碎機 , 以及一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是要走到垃圾漩渦那裡 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 然後開始撿起塑膠 , 把塑膠磨成碎片 , 再把它磨成磚塊 , 在未開發的社區中 , 可能用來當建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過垃圾漩渦的人談談 , 他們開始研究海洋環境的塑膠問題 , 一路上我發現清理塑膠的塑膠 , 相對於全世界每天實際上產生的塑膠量來說 , 我必須退一步 , 去看看更大的狀況 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更重要的是:我們需要找出一種方法 , 來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要停止使用一次就丟棄的塑膠產品這些塑膠每天以全球性的規模侵入海裏
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我關心的不只是塑膠你想象的在太平洋的中間的現在有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦可能是全球五大洋中部的塑膠垃圾
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我關心的不只是這些塑膠垃圾的漩渦還有超市裡的塑膠垃圾漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 吃的所有食物都是塑膠包裝 ,
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都以塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裏的塑膠還有從塑膠容器滲出的毒素 , 到我們體內及體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群在研究這個問題的人一起合作 , 我們成立了 「 塑膠污染聯盟 」 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多倡議我們正在進行 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海裡找到的垃圾裏百分之八十到九十都是塑膠那麽我們就稱之為 「 它是什麼 」
