recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	資源回收 , 每個人似乎都結束了他們的書籍 , 內容是關於永續、綠化 , 並帶著回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	把一些東西放到垃圾桶裡 , 然後就不用再想到了 。
what is the reality of that ?	的真實情況是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比例不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入探究 , 尤其是塑膠瓶大部分只能降級回收、焚化、甚至運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	被降級回收並作成較少的產品 。 而玻璃瓶又可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 又或者再次被用於塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們在看的另一件事是請大家想想我們在 「 減量、重覆使用、回收 」 前面增加了第四個圈 , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	盡可能地拒絕用過即丟的塑膠品
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 , 有些還是很老的學年 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在收集這些涼爽的pyrex貨櫃並使用這些來取代高價貨櫃來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶也很容易 , 如果你去旅行 , 卻忘了帶一個不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 或過濾水 , 相對的 , 購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想對在座各位說的是我也知道在座各位知道許多關於這議題的了解 , 是海洋裡很大的問題 , 但這是身為消費者的我們所創造的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由喚起大家的意識來解決這問題 , 並教導人們選擇一些替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇單次使用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這個幹掉的幹線切割成我們的海洋 , 藉此 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這場pattiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室做示範 , pranavmistry在ted的雜誌上做示範 。 這是一個戴型裝置 , 配上一個投影機 , 為我們所處的環境鋪路 。 想像一下 " 關鍵報告 " , 然後 , 一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範、設計、界面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂摩斯和帕納•米特里•格萊森特•第六森森特 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 像是我們能否進化出或發展出第六感 。 一種讓我們能夠無縫接觸、容易取得資料代謝或現存資料的能力 , 可能是相關的 , 來協助我們做出對的決定 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會認為 , 現今的手機不就已經做到這點嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與別人會面時這是最好的網路環境當然在年中你不會和某人握手然後說: 「 你能不能等一下我拿出手機然後google一下你呢 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你到超級市場 , 站在那巨大的走道上 , 各種衛生紙 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 連上一個網站 , 試著決定各種不同的衛生紙中哪個購買選擇是最環保的 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們無法很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 及採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能輕易取得這些資訊 , 而不需要使用者改變他們的任何行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	而我在這裡要揭露我們最近的努力 , 也是到目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這仍然是個過程中的成果 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我身上正戴著這個裝置我們有點有點把它和架上零件拼湊在一起順便一提 , 這裝置目前的成本只有350美元
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我帶著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一台可攜式、用電池來驅動的投影系統 , 只有一面小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些零件傳達了我口袋裡的手機 , 它扮演了通訊和計算的裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•密絲利 , 他真的是一位天才 , 一直在執行和設計這個系統 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何平面前使用手和投影在他面前的資訊進行互動
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻顯著手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著各位可能認得的簡單馬克筆蓋 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上可以追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他做出的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他可以直接去一幅長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具代表性的手勢例如 " 拍照 " , 然後拍照你面前的事物
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	然後當他走回媒體實驗室 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前將他拍的照片投影出來 , 瀏覽並整理它們 , 然後再畫出它們 。 同樣地 , 他也使用了所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前你們有些人可能也來了看過了傑夫•韓所做的示範或許有人會想 , " 這不是很像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? "
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然的手勢互動 , 兩隻手 , 諸如此類 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但它的不同點在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何平面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可用 , 和這個投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 也可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要不同點是 , 它完全是流動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點是量產後它的成本不會高於現今的手機而且也不會像是一個更大的包裝看起來會比我脖子上掛的版本還要時髦的多
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們其中一些人實踐幻想 , 像tomcruise的 「 關鍵報告 」 一樣酷 , 之所以我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮 , 是因為它真的可以扮演六感裝置中的其中之一 , 它給予你有關你面前事物的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超級市場準備購買一些紙巾
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品-這個系統可以辨識出他拿到的產品 , 用的是圖像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求加入更多的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 在他的個人標準下 , 這個選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想買加入最多漂白劑的衛生紙而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以取得亞馬遜書局的評分 。 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是朱恩的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜得到很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納轉了這本書的頁面 , 然後再看到更多關於這本書的資訊 , 像是這本書的讀者評論 , 也許還能以他最喜歡的評論來提供資訊等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁 , 他會找到我們一位朋友的註解 , 給他額外的資訊 , 說明那個特定的頁面是什麼 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時--它從來不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收到關於你閱讀的事件的影片註解 , 可以取得最新的體育分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個較有爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與別人互動時 , 也許你會看到一團團的標籤和那個人相關的字在他們的部落格及個人網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的航班延誤 , 登機門已改變等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在是什麼時候 , 就跟在手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在開發的第六感 , 讓我們無縫接觸這些有關我們可能遇到的事情的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到這麼多掌聲因為我覺得他這三個月來其實沒有睡多少 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也對他不太高興
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它現在還不夠完美 , 還差得遠 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	又有誰知道 , 或許十年過後我們會帶著植入腦內的終極第六感來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲莉絲•羅德里格茲和阿克•埃瓦菲有強大的友誼 , 生於無法想像的失去之際 。 羅德里奎茲的兒子在世界貿易中心於2001年9月11日被殺 。 埃瓦菲的兒子zacariasmoussaui被定罪於那些攻擊中的角色 , 並且正在服役生命的句子 。 希望找到和平的希望這兩個母親能明白這兩個 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題 ,
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	九一一的療癒:能找到寬恕的母親 , 友誼 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉絲•羅德里格斯:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為的不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說卻是很自然的 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道我的兒子是在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到36小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼事以我們兒子之名---我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 以及我的家人
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	我看到它時 , 卻受到了震驚 , 震驚 , 和我們生命中那可怕的爆炸 , 簡直就是 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑 , 如果罪名成立的話 , 我和我的丈夫對公開反對這說法 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那也透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者家屬一起被聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時也走過來 , 我心想: 「 真是一個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想見見那名女子 , 讓我更堅強 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍在深深的哀傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有這份力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道總有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當別人聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上就有同情心 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子所被指控的事 , 她沒有得到這樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦是等同於我 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年十一月見面 , 現在aicha會告訴你那是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	女士們先生們 , 艾波菲:午安 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我去接觸受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看見菲莉絲 , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這個團體裡唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼睛看到她也是一個母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為一個母親 , 我遭受很大的痛苦
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲的時候失去了一個孩子 , 在我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以對zacarias的故事實在是太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然痛苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的痛苦是其他女性所帶來的正面影響 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以貢獻 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性這是為我們 , 為我們女人為我們的孩子
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我講反抗暴力 , 反抗恐怖主義 ,
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的伊斯蘭女孩講說令她們不去接受那些不符自己意願的早婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免她們和我一樣結婚、受苦 , 那麼 , 這是一些好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我在aicha身上學到很多東西 , 從那天開始我們第一次見到其他的家庭成員---這是一個很私密的會議 , 因為那時是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們很害怕當時國家裡的超級愛國主義---我們這些家庭成員們 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想見我們呢 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著 , 她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	" 為什麼我們想見她呢 ? "
what did we want from each other ?	我們互相想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們就已經擁抱了 , 流淚了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們坐成一個圓圈 , 尋求協助 , 來自人們在這種和解中所體驗到的 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	由aicha成立 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你 , 我是如何為你家中所發生的事感到抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎樣的難受我認為 , 如果這是一個罪行那個人應該得到公平的審判及懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她就是那樣接觸我們 , 我想說 , 這是個破冰者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	那時發生的事 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 我們都作為人而被連繫著 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在那個下午完結的時候---大概是午餐後的三小時---我們覺得好像彼此都已經認識了一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 不只是一個女人 , 在現今的情況下 , 能夠如此慷慨大方 , 以及當時是什麼 , 還有她兒子所過的 , 還有她過去的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過有人有著如此艱苦的人生 , 來自這麼完全不同的文化和環境 , 來自我自己的 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的連繫 , 我非常重視這種聯繫 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都和對方感到害怕有關 , 但走出這一步接著發現: 「 嘿 , 這並沒有那麼困難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	還有誰能不認識 , 或是跟我很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以下結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	笑聲〈傳譯〉aw:我想說我們必須試著去認識其他人 , 其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也必須要寬容 , 你的心念必須要寬容 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界太多無法取得乾淨的飲用水了 。 工程師麥可普立查對它做了點什麼 , 發明了可攜式生命體的過濾器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內得到最多可飲用水 。 這是2009年tedglobal的驚人示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、展示、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源 。

the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受那在研討會提供給你們的水 , 在過去的幾天裡
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	而且我相信你們會覺得這是來自一個安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果它不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是從這樣的來源
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	根據統計 , 你們之中有一半的人可能患有痢疾 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過很多關於統計和提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎是無法通過
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 用當前的想法 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 以致於無法思索解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們立即關閉:我們、政府、和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓大家以不同的角度思考問題已經被解決了
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全球各地又有13 , 000人正在腹瀉中受苦 。
and four children have just died .	而且四個孩子剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶是因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我跟你們一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節的隔天 , 看著電視上不斷報導南亞海嘯摧毀性的新聞 , 電視上不斷播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	在接下來的數週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 要不然就面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的令我無法忘懷 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國衝著而來 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道這花了五天 , 才能把水運到超市嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 只為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時 , 我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	接下來的幾個月 , 我花了很多時間在車庫裡 , 還有我廚房裡的廚房 , 令我太太很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型後 , 我終於做出了這個─lifesaver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好了 , 現在來談一下科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌就差不多200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	那肯定會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水瓶裡有15奈米大小 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有什麼能度過的 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好了 , 我現在要給你們展示一些

okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 那我要把這些非常骯髒的水 , 放進這裏來 。 你們還想喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 , 可以了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些打氣筒 , 好嗎 ?

now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	現在只要我拉開它的茶 , 無菌的飲用水將會流出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快一點 。 準備好了嗎 ?

and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 利用故障安全技術 , 這個系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把內筒取出 , 換一個新的進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	還要再花6 , 000公升
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看它的應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統來說 , 危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個星期後 , 我們建立營地 ,
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取用安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病會傳播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會自行延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但只要用不同的方式思考 , 再運送這些東西 , 大家就可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 並開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 不需要天然災害才可行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	以舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工程的費用實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上運算這些數字時 , 你的指數就用完了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡有一些 「 不同的思維 」 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做、使用大自然、她有絕佳的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從這裏提水 , 免費除去水中鹽分 , 運送到那裏 , 傾倒在山地、河川、以及溪流中 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的只是將它消毒而已 。 我們要怎麼做到 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或是使用這種
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 用的是jerry罐頭
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將能處理二萬五千公升的水 ; 這足夠一個四歲、三年的家庭使用 。
and how much does it cost ?	到底要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約只需半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 以不同的方式思考 , 在使用的時候就用水 , 母親和孩子不用再每天漫步四小時來取得他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的水源取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只需要八十億美元 , 我們就可以達到千禧目標的目標 , 目標是要讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	將上述套入此情況 , 英國政府每年花約120億英鎊於國外援助 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要就此罷手 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 結果是每年因此受苦的三十五億人和死去的兩百萬個兒童會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪阿什唐聲稱我們正活在歷史上的這個時刻 , 權力正在以從未有的方式改變中 。 在tedxbrussels的一個咒語演講中 , 他提出了他將要面臨的三個重大轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化文化
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪阿什唐:全球勢力轉移的現象
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一位很有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代 , 邱吉爾的腦部迴盪
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: " 在夏日的idle山 , 躺著在溪流之中 , 我聽到了遠方的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲音 , 遙遠的 , 低沉的 , 高聳的在路上 , 親愛的 , 親愛的朋友和食物來到粉末 , 士兵遊走很快就要死了 。 "
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些感興趣的詩人 , 這首詩是夏俄羅斯小姐的詩作 , 作者是豪斯曼的作品 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所知道的 , 也在尼爾森交響曲中也聽到了 , 十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱 , 遍地林木的夏天穩定 , 即將告一段落 , 我們即將進入歷史上那些恐怖的階段之一 , 當權力轉移的時候 ,
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些時期總是伴隨著騷動 , 伴隨著騷動 , 還有很多時候都是血腥的 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我要傳達的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 那時 , 權力已開始改變 , 世界新的外貌 , 世界存在的新權力正在慢慢成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些也是--我們今天很清楚的看到--幾乎總是非常動盪的時刻 , 極為困難的時刻 , 而且往往都是非常血腥的時刻 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便提一下 , 這發生在每個世紀一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生時--那是豪斯曼當時的感受--也就是 , 邱吉爾也同樣感受到 , 當權力從老國 , 歐洲舊勢力通過大西洋時期 , 橫跨了大西洋 , 到美國新興強國時期的美國 , 也就是美國本世紀初期 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被人耍了兩個血腥的災難就在那最後一個世紀兩場災難分別是兩次的世界大戰
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 用比較精確的方式來描述他們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們正處於這樣的時代
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	在這之中 , 前兩項是關於權力移轉
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	而第二個 , 是關於我想要談的新維度 , 它從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但我們來談談權力轉移到世界各地
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事 , 在一種意義上 , 非常可怕 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見過了橫向的權力移轉希臘的權力傳到羅馬以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力移轉但我們看到的有些微的不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移轉 ,
it's also moving vertically .	也有直向移轉
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今所發生的權力 , 受到責任的牽制也受到法律的牽制現在國家的機構已開始大量地遷移至全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力雖然我們說是全球化市場但事實上 , 卻是全球化權力
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級權力被賦予法律責任歸屬於國際舞台上則否 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台也是現在存在權力的全球舞台:互聯網的力量、衛星廣播的力量、貨幣的力量、和流動巨大貨幣的力量、以及流轉的貨幣有32倍的金錢預算、應該有的權力 , 來融資變革、或是去幫助那些近期將我們所有人帶到我們的膝蓋內的金融預算大國度 , 所擁有的預算數目比中型國家還要高32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些住在一個全球化的空間幾乎沒有法律規範也沒有法律規範這些人行為可能沒有受到限制
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這種適應力強大到瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	那些最有權力在沒有限制的空間裡營運的人 , 總是很適合 。 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有規範的空間 , 會變成充斥的 , 不只是你想要的國際貿易 , 網路等等 。 還有很多你不想要的 , 國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是即使你是世界上最強勢的國家儘管如此 , 那些生活在空間裡的人還是可以攻擊你甚至在九月的一個早晨中攻擊你
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說大約是這四百萬美金中的六成被用來資助911恐怖攻擊的金融機構通過雙子星大樓 , 911摧毀的高樓 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人用這樣的空間大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播的空間 , 來處理他們的毒藥 , 那重點在於破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早有一天 , 早晚有一天 , 歷史的統治者就是權力取向統治者必須遵從 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰之一就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年 , 或多或少會是暴動的程度 , 或多或少會是我們可以達成的目標:將統治者帶上國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談要設立全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我的看法是 , 女士們先生們這是不大可能的做法是他們設立更多聯合國的機構
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就必須發明
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要的是一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種手段 , 讓你能夠將國際行動合理化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但是 , 一談到治理全球空間我猜 , 這不會發生在更多聯合國的機構
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	權力將會實現 , 成為以條約為基礎的制度、以條約為基礎的協議 , 共同治理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你仔細看 , 你會發現他們正在發生 , 已經開始浮現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為底的合約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到足以支撐最強大的美國 , 甚至在必要時還會考量到 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:努力想創立一個合約為底的組織
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道我們必須組一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間的機構為了財務上的推論
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團因而建立的 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題了 , 我們等一下就會回到這裡 , 那就是 , 如果你把最有權力的人聚集在一起 , 來制定以條約為基礎的制度規則 , 來填補統治空間 , 那麼 , 對於那些被排除的弱者會有什麼後果 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	那是個大問題 , 我們馬上就會回到這問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你正經歷這些動亂的時期 , 或多或少會有騷動 , 那麼我們成功的做法 , 會大大取決於我們把合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	和看著這開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和觀眾談這類的事情 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還會橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你或許會反駁你所說的文明歷史這些文明都聚集在海洋四周最先到達的地中海區域又是近期西方強國的後裔
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在正目睹了權力的根本轉變 , 廣泛說 , 遠離那些聚集在大西洋岸邊的國家 , 轉向那些聚集在太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這從經濟實力開始 , 但是 , 總是如此 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增在世界上日漸成長的其他強權國家中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這實際上不是太大的轉變 , 從西方轉到東方 , 不太一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測結果是 , 美國在未來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是世界上最強的國家 , 但她權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 這樣的情況已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正要走出五十年 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 在這個歷史中 , 我們所擁有的是一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一方針對同伴的每一方都必須被他的立場引用 , 來對抗華盛頓這個世界 , 一個被一個獨立自主的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這在歷史上卻不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在所出現的是關於歷史的普通案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你們即將看到多極世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特色 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會成為最強權的國家 , 但在越來越多的多極化世界中 , 他們卻是最強權的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你會開始看到中國其他權力建設中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是 , 中國要成為偉大的核心 , 並不平穩 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	這會是相當嚴峻的 , 因為中國在自由經濟後開始對她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度、巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你逐漸看到 , 實際上 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來更像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一位偉大的英國外交大臣 , 坎寧閣下 , 曾用 「 歐洲人的權力協調 」 來形容它 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	達到一種平衡 , 五方面的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國人總是在玩平衡
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來建立對應的平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這個被壟斷的世界裡 , 你有固定的同盟國 , 北約組織 , 華約組織 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定對立的權力代表著同盟國 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有兩方面的兩極性意味著同盟國的改變和改變 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們即將進入的世界 , 我們逐漸會看到我們的盟友並不是固定不變的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有一個共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們也會越來越常見到 , 即使我們西方國家也會展開 , 不得不伸出大西洋的舒適圈圈 , 與他人結盟 , 如果我們想要在世上做事 ,
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	值得注意的是 , 當我們進入利比亞的時候 , 光靠西方國家是不夠好的 ; 我們不得不帶著其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們得帶來 , 在這個例子中 , 阿拉伯聯盟
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗 , 也是西方最後一次獨自嘗試這麼做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是我們已經達到了400年後的開端 , 我說400年後的鄂圖曼帝國的終結 , 終結了西方強權國家的霸權 , 西方的機構和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能團結在一起 , 它可以提出、丟棄在世界的每個角落 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	就拿最近二次世界大戰後發生的金融危機為例 ,
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織布雷頓森林機構解決問題
now we have to call in others .	現在我們得打電話到其他人面前
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造二十國集團
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須跨出我們西方朋友的舒適圈
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	我來為你們做個預測 , 預測結果可能會更嚇人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑現在已經400年以後西方國家的勢力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	有人對我說: 「 中國絕對不會參與什麼在世界上建立和平的活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 , 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊服役於藍色貝雷區下 , 服役於藍色旗幟 , 服役於聯合國的指令下 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	海軍對付索馬利亞海盜最大的海軍艦隊在哪裡 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	他們當然是 , 他們是一個慈善主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要維持航道暢通
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們沒有共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 和誰 , 在當下 , 我們要和他們分享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是個全新的角度來看這個正在浮現的新世界
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不一樣 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們現代社會 , 因為有網際網路 , 因為人們在這裡談論過的各種事物 , 所有事物都有關連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是以國家、個人的身分 , 以一種前所未有的方式 , 互相連結著 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關係 , 那一直都是存在的
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們是緊密地連接在一起
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你會在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 24小時後 , 查爾斯戴高樂機場就成了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉 , 整個大崩離 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的食物暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深入地彼此連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這也就是說 , 一個國家獨自行動的概念 , 不與他人接觸、不和他人合作 , 而是不再是一個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動 , 並不侷限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家自己來控制自己的國土 , 因為國外的影響已經開始影響到國家內部的變化 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我年輕的時候曾在大英帝國戰爭時當過兵
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 國防剛好是一回事我們的軍隊多強 , 我們的空軍多厲害我們的海軍陸戰隊多厲害我們的同盟國多厲害
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在圍牆外的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人則在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在如果我想談談我國防部 , 我得和衛生署談談因為傳染病對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得和農業部長談談因為食物安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得和工業部長談談因為高科技公共設施的脆弱性現在是我們的敵人攻擊點 , 正如我們從網路戰爭上所看到的──我得和內政部談談 , 當時正因為那些已經進入我們國家的人住在我們的都市的人住在我們的都市 , 我們的房子的人對話 , 都有直接的影響 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只是一個士兵和國防部的問題 ,
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	是它的能力可以將它的機構鎖在一起 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴各位一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直架構的 , 建構在工業革命時代的經濟模式上 , 垂直架構上 , 分工的任務 , 指揮結構把錯的結構弄錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在座的各位女士們 , 在座的各位 , 你們都知道 , 我們這個時代的典範結構就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	是你網絡的能力很重要無論是你政府內部還是外部都很重要
so here is ashdown's third law .	下面是下面第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明出來 , 第三定律總是比較好聽 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	下面的第三個法則是:在現代 , 所有東西都連結在一起 , 對於你能做的事 , 最重要的是你能和他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊軍隊 , 不論你是否是企業人 , 是你的關鍵點、你的內部人士、你和別人聯絡的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業中 , 你了解這一點 ; 政府不了解 。
but now one final thing .	但現在還有最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在就以一種前所未有的方式 , 和以前完全不一樣的方式聯繫在一起 , 那這也是我們和彼此有著相同目標的情況 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間且是史上頭一遭 , 集體防禦 , 它主宰了我們來保護國家的概念 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去是這樣如果我的部落比他們的強 , 我就安全了如果我的國家比他們的強 , 我就安全了我的盟國 , 像是北約組織 , 比他們同盟的強 , 我就安全了
it is no longer the case .	已經不再是
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯和大規模毀滅性武器的出現意味著我和敵人有著相同的命運
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	1970年代 , 當我還是外交官在日內瓦和蘇聯協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解 , 我們和他們有著相同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是沒有用的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著相同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一項要素是以色列和巴勒斯坦人不了解他們有集體的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士 , 過去幾年來有遠見者和詩人所提出的建言 , 轉變成我們得要認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 最後將以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	johndonne's的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 請不要為打鐘的誰發出 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它說: 「 每個人的死亡都對我有影響 , 因為我也有參與人類活動 , 不去問鐘聲告訴誰 , 鐘聲為你帶來了影響 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•多恩來說 , 道德的建議是
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們 , 我認為 , 屬於我們生存的方程式 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到延長壽命和健康的路徑 , danbuetner和團隊在研究世界上的 「 藍色慢活區 」 , 這些社區的長輩和活力 , 記錄了tedxtc的年齡 。 他共享9個常見的飲食習慣和生活方式 , 讓它們可以在100歲時轉播 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個叫做丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實在某種生物限制下人平均能活多久只有百分之十是基因所決定
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由生活方式決定
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能得出一個實際的方法來增長壽命
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的方法是什麼他們大概說不出來
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法或阿金減肥法
you have the usda food pyramid .	有美國農業部食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	歐茲博士告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實上 , 許多混淆存在於真正幫助我們活得更長久的方法之上 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品 , 你應該接受嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白葵呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	並且有目的性地參與其中嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神上呢 ? 我們又該如何與人交流 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理界線分明的區塊
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後把一組專家帶進來用這個方法仔細地講述這些人的行為 , 提煉出跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想先揭穿一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你很努力 , 就能活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然這是美國人口成長最快的國家卻很難達到一百歲
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是長壽的計劃 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計成一種叫做成功繁衍的東西 。
i love that word .	我愛這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學的日子
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把繁衍的成功定義為:你有孩子的年齡 , 然後下一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在這種進化的效應完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	假如你是哺乳類 , 假如你是隻老鼠或是大象或人 , 在兩者之間都是相同的
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要活到一百歲 , 你不僅得有個非常好的生活方式 , 你還得抽中基因頭彩 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有療法可以幫助緩慢、逆轉、甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有九十九件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太激烈 , 膝蓋的軟骨也碎裂 , 軟骨也不回來了 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 , 腦斑會沉積在腦裡我們還會得老年癡呆症
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有三十五兆個細胞 , 兆個有著 「 t 」 的細胞 , 我們在這裡談的是國債 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會轉一圈 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次他們把自己的傷害翻過來 , 就會造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數方式增加增長
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都擁有披頭四或老鷹合唱團的唱片我們會拷貝一份到錄音帶上 , 讓朋友複製錄音帶而且很快地 , 代代相傳錄音帶就聽起來像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個六十五歲的人老化的速度比一個十二歲的人快一百二十五倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你無法減緩或停止老化 , 那我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的容量 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約可用九十年 , 女人則多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在那條線的某處 , 我們在那邊留下了大約十二年美好的年份 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年可以讓我們
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示多年來大多都不會出現慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些消失的最佳方式 , 就是看看世界各地文化的實際經驗 , 讓人們活到一百歲的比率 , 比我們高出十倍以上 , 預期壽命多了十多年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍寶地在義大利海岸外約一百二十五英哩處 , 薩丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 而是高地上 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們看到的是男人活的最長壽百歲人瑞的數目大約是美國的十倍
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不僅活到一百歲而已他們還十分有活力
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作砍柴 , 還能打敗比自己年輕六十歲的小夥子
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上能回溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是個與世隔絕的青銅器文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為那裡的土地非常不孕 , 幾乎都是牧羊人 , 那裡有時是規律、低強度的體力活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主特別是能帶到田裡的食物
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做catamica , 用硬粒小麥製作的一種乳酪 , 來自青草餵養的動物所以這種乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸而是一種葡萄酒 , 它的多酚含量比世界所知的任何酒都多三倍
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但是我想真正的秘密 , 在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎二十四歲就到頂點了 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告就知道
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你的年紀越高 , 你的智慧就越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你的老化父母有益 , 還能讓他們和家人保持距離 , 平均壽命四到六年 , 研究顯示這對那些家庭的小孩也有益處 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 疾病的比率也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現地球另一端的第二個藍寶地 , 位於東京南方八百英里處 , 位在琉球的群島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是一百六十一個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而主島的北端是世界長壽的原點
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個能找到最老老的女性群體的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有著世界上最長而無障礙的預期壽命
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	活很久 , 往往在睡夢中死去 , 非常快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在做愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多快活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的結腸癌和乳癌案例是美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	而心血管疾病的比例是我們的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這個文化產生了這些數字 , 很明顯地 , 他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	同樣地 , 植物為主的飲食富有多種顏色的蔬菜
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而且他們吃大約八倍的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們所吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小小的策略要避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們吃下小盤子 , 所以每次用餐攝取較少的卡路里 ,
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不要以家庭風格為服務 , 你可以隨心所欲地吃你說話的樣子 , 他們在櫃檯上菜 , 把食物拿走 , 然後再把食物送到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句流傳三千年的格言我認為是飲食建議中最棒的
it was invented by confucius .	由孔子所發明
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 " 騷擾 , 霍奇 , butchi "
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	其實就是這些人在用餐前說的一句話來提醒自己吃到八分飽就好
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	飽足感要花半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住吃到八分飽就好幫助你免於做這些事
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構跟長壽相關
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會害死人
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在減少到一半
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你會生在一種體系裡讓你自動擁有半打朋友與他們共同生活
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為模合 。 假如你處於某個模合走運時 , 別人會期待你去分享假如你運氣不好、孩子生病、父母去世總有人會在背後支持你
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個 「 模合 」 , 這五位女士相處了九十七年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是一百零二歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部份 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作、有生產力的地方 ,
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 碰 , 我們退休
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這指的就是在簡單的椅子上退休 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而是有個詞佔了你一生 , 這個詞是 「 生而有之 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大致翻譯: 「 早上起床的理由 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道師父來說他的生存價值就是拿著這位武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說就是持續為他的家人釣魚每週三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	國家老化研究院提出這個問題 , 給我們一份問卷調查 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們對問卷的文化都非常敏感 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼一覺醒來
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生存價值不過就在於她的曾曾曾孫女
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個年齡段相隔101歲半的女孩
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著自己的曾曾曾孫女
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 這感覺就像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這想法很棒 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我找到美國的藍寶地
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有陣子我們將目光放在明尼蘇達的草原那裡百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但是因為所有的年輕人都離開了
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料 ,
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的人口 , 是基督復臨安息日會的教友集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的衛理專家
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落日落裡從世界各地慶祝自己的安息日是星期六到日落
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的避難所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	而且他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達著他們相對來說非常長壽的訊息 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	美國的預期壽命是八十歲
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但基督復臨派的女教友她們的預期壽命是八十九
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很傑出的研究 。 而且我認為這大大說明了這個藍色慢活區計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個多種族的社區
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套生活小習慣他們一生中大部分時間都習慣於儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中拿取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九節上帝談到豆子和種子另一節則是談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個避難所 ,
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每個禮拜二十四小時不管多忙 , 工作壓力多大還要讓孩子們停下一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路然後 , 在宗教的版圖上 , 天生就走路了
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處不在於偶爾為之而在於 , 權力是每週持續一生的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往跟其他教徒來往
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的聚會 , 你不會看到人們揮舞著jimbeam或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在說下一次的自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們禱告 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的人
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁可是當包商想要六千美金來建造隱私的圍籬時他說: 「 為了這類的錢 , 我就自己幹 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把欄杆拖來拖去
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預料的是 , 可能在第四天他會被送進手術室
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人而是做開心手術的人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲的他仍然每個月做20次開心手術 ,
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲是一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上才開始游泳
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 把公雞尾巴吐出來 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天的舉重開始
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年的塞維利亞卡提卡拉凱迪拉克被送往聖博納迪諾州高速公路她在那裡依然是七個不同組織的志工
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加十九次冒險活動 ,
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一你認識的人裡不塗防曬霜還會騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠的人
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何探險比坐馬奇•狄頓機車更恐怖的了 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒遇到的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三個文化裡有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼事是他們全都做的 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的歸結為九項
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後 , 我們又進行了兩次藍寶地遠征 , 而這些共同的探險家依然適用於此 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項我即將要提出一項悖論就是他們都不運動至少是我們所認為的運動
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立起的生活讓他們一直投入身體活動
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人她們坐在地板上 , 起身又坐下一天三、四十回
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在直立的房子裡樓梯上下
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個可以表達出院工作或家事的按鈕可按
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想攪拌蛋糕 , 他們會用手
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里跟跑步機一樣多
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們進行刻意的身體活動時 , 這是他們所享受的東西 。 他們傾向行走 , 這是唯一證實能延遲認知的衰退的方法 , 他們往往有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式安排他們的生活 , 所以他們有對的觀點 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都花時間在下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 督復臨派教徒祈禱
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人敬祖
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕時間或壓力大 , 會引發一種發炎反應 , 這種反應跟很多病相關 , 從老年癡呆到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘便會將該發炎的狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙來表達目的感 , 像琉球人的 「 生存感 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道自己生命最危險的兩年是出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率還有退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感並且在生活中活化這價值大約是七年的預期壽命
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天都小飲一點 , 不適合賣給美國的人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們的飲食往往以植物為主
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是吃很多豆類跟堅果
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略保持過度飲食 , 一些小事在對的時間將他們從桌子上推開 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎是它們連結的方式 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一照顧好小孩跟年邁父母
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 這價值四到十四年額外的預期壽命假如你維持一個月四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	其中最嚴重的是他們也屬於右派族群
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就遇到對的人就是他們積極結交正確
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機率會變胖
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 假如你跟不健康的人來往隨著時間就會有顯著的影響
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友對休閒的想法是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點酒 , 但不多 , 他們吃得對 , 且他們有參與感 , 且值得信任和值得信任 , 那會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	節食沒用 , 在世界歷史上沒有一個飲食適用人口為2%以上
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始十月就結束
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽並沒有短期的方案 , 不論是藥物或其他東西 , 都一樣 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最有意義的事 , 來為你的生命增加年歲和人生增添生命 。 謝謝大家 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水導電 ; 一扇窗戶從明顯轉成開關的翻轉窗 ; 一種製造音樂的果凍 。 所有這些東西都有 , 卡塔琳娜.莫塔說:該是把電玩了 。 莫塔帶領我們參觀了一場令人驚訝又酷的新材料 , 暗示我們要知道它們有什麼好處 , 去實驗、修改、有趣的 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力 , 設計 , 科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩弄智慧型材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父將腳踏車和洗衣機改裝成一台車以便載送家人
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做既是因為沒錢買車也是因為他知道如何改裝
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經 , 我們知道東西是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠建造、修理它們 , 或至少明智地做出決定 , 決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多diy的做法在二十世紀下半葉喪生 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創建社群以及開放模型正將東西的運作及其原料等知識逐漸帶回我們的生活中而我相信我們需要更進一步去了解事物的組成
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的又是如何生產的
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚嘆又有未來感的複合材料塑膠能夠改變形狀 , 能夠導電 , 顏料會改變顏色 , 和會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不需要用傳統印刷電路或電線而可以直接油漆電路
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小例子 , 我們用它來製造一個觸控感應器 , 它會透過打開這個小光來對我的皮膚作反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家一直都在使用導電油墨 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上面 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是說 , 雖然普通丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光但這一具會在我開燈的時候整個表面都會發光
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料有兩個已知的應用 , 其中包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下變色
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我要把這個東西放在裝在熱的盤子上 , 溫度只比環境低一點點 , 大家可以看到結果 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	因此 , 這種材料的其中一個主要應用是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它意味著內容物是否涼爽可以飲用 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是我們所知的智慧型材料中的一小部分 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	再過幾年 , 它們就會被用在我們日常所使用的許多物品和技術上 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車但我們可以有可以依據溫度變化的牆壁可以捲起來的鍵盤一關就能變不透明的窗戶
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以我是個社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要來這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對東西的運作感到好奇以及它們是如何製成的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該要對構成我們世界的這些組成要素有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些將成為我們未來的高科技複合材料還不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	如何使用它們幾乎沒有什麼資訊 , 也幾乎沒有人知道它們是如何產生的 。
