so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以目前 , 它們幾乎存在於貿易機密和專利當中 , 只有大學和企業能取得的 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , 我和克絲蒂•波義耳開始一項我們稱之為材料公開化的計劃
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	在這個網站中 , 我們以及任何想要加入的人都可以分享實驗成果 , 發表資訊鼓勵他人隨時都可以貢獻一己之力並聚集研究資源比如 , 研究論文和輔導 , 由其他像我們一樣的製作者來進行
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個龐大、集體創建的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料製造這些diy資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為什麼我們應該要關心智慧型材料的運作方式以及組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造自己不了解的東西 , 最後我們卻不了解且使用的東西卻塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 穿的衣服住的房子 , 全都對我們的行為健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該去認識和理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是創新總是以修補匠為燃料
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 而不是專家 , 一直都是登山腳踏車的發明家和改進者 , 包括半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學非常複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但也不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩名科學家便深知這一點當他們發表一篇論文用的是比較簡單的方法用來製作導電油墨
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克在那之前完全沒有化學經驗 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間進行實驗 , 只使用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據其他科學家的說明書自製試管震盪器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上公開了他的研究成果包含所有他嘗試過的但沒有成功所以其他人可以研究並重現成果
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 喬登最主要的創新形式是把在芝加哥一間設備精良的實驗室中所發明的實驗 , 在他自己製造的車庫中 , 只用很便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項成果 , 其他人可以查到他要去的地方 , 劃出更簡單的步驟 , 改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	我想提到的另一個例子是強調材料的特質同時著重建造者的創意與技巧
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子零件在教導我們認識東西的運作上非常強大 , 但限制在它們的設計上 , 會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的作法是規劃一系列的技術用來創造不尋常的物品使我們能不受限於設計上的限制所教導的素材本身
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗裡 , 這是我最喜歡的作品之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3播放器和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜用各式各樣的材料製作出一系列的紙喇叭
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登以及許多其它的製作者漢娜將她的食譜公開讓任何人可以複製或複製
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子只是現在前景最被看好的材料科學其中一個分支罷了紙電子讓我們能創造出更便宜、靈活的電子產品
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝成品 , 以及她分享發現的事實 , 打開了一連串極具美感以及創新的新可能的大門 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們的熱情和好奇心所創造出來的 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常從獨特的角度解決問題 , 並在過程中發現替代方案或更好的方式 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人在材料上做實驗越多研究人員願意分享研究散播知識我們就越有機會創造出服務眾人的科技
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像泰德尼爾森在一九七零年代早期寫下 「 現在你必須要了解電腦 」 時的心情
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大架構 , 沒人敢想也能在家裡有一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你們現在必須要了解智慧型材料 , 有點奇怪 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要記住 , 取得關於新興科技的先發知識是確保我們在創造未來時最好的說法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們駕駛時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡 , 鎖定門鎖 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 引導我們 , 即使我們只能看見前方和後方的幾輛車 。 但如果汽車可以彼此分享他們立場和速度的資料 , 並且使用預測模型來計算馬路上所有人最安全的路徑 ? 珍妮佛.洛伊想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果汽車可以說話意外可能是可以避免的
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不願去想的事但現實中我們在世界各地看到汽車儀表板上的宗教畫像和運氣好的圖示背叛我們知道這是事實
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而當中百分之七十五的車禍和毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	當時我還年輕在高速公路上 , 前面的車輛 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在停車 , 停車 , 高速公路上就停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	那時只剩65比0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	踩著煞車
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	abs系統啟動了但車仍向前駛車繼續向前我知道車不會停了氣囊彈出車子毀了幸好沒有人受傷
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車會停我認為我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 只要讓我們的車子可以相互交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想請各位回想一下現在開車的體驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上車關上門在一個玻璃泡裡
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的軀殼裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在看不清路面的情況下在其他的金屬巨人之間穿梭在超高速公路上
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	可以嗎 ? 你只需要引導你的是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這是你唯一擁有的 , 眼睛不是設計來完成這個任務的 , 但之後人們請你做類似的事情 , 你想要換條車道 , 他們要求你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	不看路面 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你前進的方向 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後駕駛下道路不檢查你的路 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人都一樣 。 這是安全駕駛的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們得要 , 我們得要做出選擇 , 我是看這裡還是這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們還是會錯過一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們感覺出錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我也相信這一點 。 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多影片 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技可以協助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車互相交換資訊我們不僅可以看到前面三部輛車還能看到後面三輛車右邊和左邊同時也可以看到鳥的眼睛我們還能看到這些車
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看車子的行進速度有多快 , 或停止的速度 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要去0 , 我就會知道了 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將可以預見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你們可能覺得這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不是 。 有了汽車 , 不是不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車是立體的有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	沿著路行駛 ,
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常在預先出版的路線上行駛
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車在近期要在哪裡 , 其實並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使當你在你的車上 , 和一些摩托車騎士在你車上時速85英里 ! 車子底下的時速85英里 , 我知道你有這段經驗 , 那個人並不 「 無中生有 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那人可能在路上走了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	是吧 ? 我是說 , 有人看過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10哩前20哩前30哩前 , 有人看到那傢伙 , 一部車看到那傢伙 , 然後把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你就會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車也會在他耳邊小聲地說 , 像是: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘機車 , 請小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對牠們很好 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一個簡單的開始 , 就好比在車與車之間分享我們車與車之間的位置資料 , 只要分享gps即可 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車上裝有gps和攝影機 , 我就能精確地知道我現在在哪裡 , 以及我現在的速度有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估算我旁邊哪裡有車 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己身在何方也能模糊地知道其他車子的位置
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子分享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會如何 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了一個電腦模擬看下列情況會產生什麼結果當用輕微的流量 , 車輛只是分享gps資訊我們把這個研究帶進了電腦模擬帶到機械試驗場 , 裡面裝有汽車感應器的裝置:立體攝影機、gps和二維雷射雷射雷射的 「 測驗 」 這些都是普遍背後的系統
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機台 , 機械人彼此聊天 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器朝彼此過來時 , 它們能追蹤到彼此的精確位置 , 它們能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你的演講太多了 , 你很難去處理所有的資料封包 , 所以你得優先順序 , 這就是預測模型會幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子在追蹤可預期的軌跡 , 你就不會去注意那些格子 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先那位看起來有點偏差的傢伙
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	就可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了 , 你要怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪些駕駛要提高警覺性 , 才能脫穎而出 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	而我們想要做的事 , 我們要如何警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲地說: 「 你得趕緊離開 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事一 , 車子的性能第二 , 駕駛的能力
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做些什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急時刻的最佳位置 ,
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一項不同的研究 , 做駕駛者的狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三部攝影機就可以偵測到駕駛正在往前看 , 往下看 , 還是向下看手機或是喝杯咖啡
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以知道是誰、是哪一部車子最好離開目前的道路去幫每個人計算最安全的路徑
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術在今天就存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為 , 我們面對的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這個想法讓人非常不安這個想法是 , 我們的車子會監視我們 , 跟其他車子說說我們會繞著路穿過一大片流言言語的潮流
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信這可以用一種保護我們隱私的方式來做 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我對你不了解你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看著你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我覺得這將是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位想一想 , 如果你真的不希望那煩人的青少年在你背後知道你要煞車 , 知道你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	很願意地分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到對每個人最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	來讓你的車八卦你
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	這會讓道路更安全
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize公司彼得.戴曼迪斯談到 , 他如何協助史蒂芬霍金去實現他的夢想 , 做法是一頭飛進大氣層 , 在0g時體驗無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短話題、空間、科技、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	在史蒂芬霍金的操作中 , 彼得•戴曼迪斯沒到史蒂芬•霍金 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道 , 我對於開創太空新領域有多麼熱衷 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可置信的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是在基因組學archonxprize的場合上 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 將頒發給第一個能於十天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因體一百個個個體 , 我們將這些基因組定序成為它的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特是那事件的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你體重為零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他當場就說: 「 當然可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要體驗零度的唯一方法 , 其實是用拋物線飛行 , 沒有重量飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	坐飛機 , 飛越頂部 , 25秒都沒有重量 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	一而再 , 再而三地做
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得知八到十分鐘的無重力經驗 , 美國太空總署訓練他們這麼久的太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始經營 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	並且宣布將要搭載史蒂芬•霍金 ,
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機關及飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想要去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了記者會 , 我們宣佈我們打算做一個無重力拋物線飛行給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切非常順利 , 我們可能會做三次拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他爲什麽他要這樣做
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他說的話對我來說非常感動
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生物面臨著不斷增加的危機可能會被災難所消滅...
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果人類不上太空的話 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他出去甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車內 , 坐落到zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	有大概20個人捐款我們募到了15萬美元作為兒童慈善事業之用他們跟著我們一起飛
a few tedsters here .	這裡幾位tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生 , 和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他血液的po2值、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們什麼事都發生了 , 萬一有緊急事件 ; 天知道 , 你不會想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的夥伴byronlichtenberg跟我小心的把他暫停為零
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	當他在那兒時 , 我們要讓他去體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很好 。 他笑著 , 我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	實際上 , 我們讓一顆漂浮著的蘋果一同入鏡以表彰艾薩克•牛頓爵士因為霍金教授在劍橋大學擔任了和牛頓相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這位先生不像65歲的輪椅男士 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一顆珍貴的珠寶上 , 它是在我們的有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入這趟壯舉般的冒險之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky展示了3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現的是細胞內的繁忙生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky賦予細胞生命
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一個醫學繪圖師 , 我的觀點和別人稍微不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 以及科學中真與美的表現方式 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然兩者本身都是很美妙的東西 , 但它們都有非常美妙的東西在追求它們 。 真和美是理想的事物 , 可以被科學和數學所檢視的真與美 , 就像是理想的連體雙胞胎 , 想要和科學家約會的 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是 「 真 」 的表示表示是敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 。 不可思議 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的、有用的有時甚至是在事後很長一段時間
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你們可以放一些圖片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	對不懂科學的人來說 , 真與美往往是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們所描述的美 , 通常只有在你了解了那些語言以及所研究的主題中 , 才能被表述出真與美的事物時 , 才能被理解 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙常數 , 在宇宙中有著人類學的理念 , 你會發現生命必然是從描述宇宙的數字進化出來的這些是非常難以理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	一直以來我想要做的是 , 既然我有一個醫學繪圖師我的動畫技術傳自我老爸 , 他也是一個雕塑家兼我的視覺導師我想找出一種方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 通過動畫、使用圖片 , 來訴說故事 , 如此一來 , 人們就不見得有證據能帶來的事物 , 也能被教導 , 並且能夠被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一種環境中 , 在這種環境中 , 他們所學習的主題包括真與美 , 但他們被教導的方式是片面的、不完整的 , 且被深深吸引到 , 在那裡 , 真與美並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的陳年食譜 , 烹煮雞肉直到香味通通散去 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不希望這樣對待我們的學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話 。 他問我我和我的團隊 , 是否有興趣改變哈佛大學的醫學與科學教育程度 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 它可以探索分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 讓學生可以了解 , 一個可以涵蓋所有事實的更大圖片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們腦海中可能有一個腦區圖 , 代表細胞是一座龐大、繁忙、複雜的城市 , 那裡充滿了微機械 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓全世界的奈米學家嫉妒 , 它們是能自我引導、強大且精確的裝置 , 它們是由胺基酸的弦所構成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓細胞移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞複製、激發我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	我們想要做的是 , 想辦法讓這個故事成爲動畫 , 這會是哈佛大學biovisions的主題 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有教授的知識 , 把一切視覺化 , 這樣這些學生將能夠從細胞內發現細胞真正的真與美 , 並且能夠通過這樣的視覺化觀 , 深入研究 , 深入了解他們的心智 , 如此一來 , 能激發他們的想像力和思想 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子的組合方式 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們想出了一個主題 , 那就是 , 巨噬細胞在微血管之間穿梭著 , 它們在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 然後從微血管壁上取得資訊 , 它們就得到了這些資訊 , 外圍某處有發炎反應 , 它們看不見也感覺得到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的信息會讓他們停止 , 使他們內化 , 必須做出各式各樣的零件 , 使他們改變形狀 , 並且試著跳脫微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家一起研究 , 以及資料庫模型 , 看出原子上正確的分子 , 並搞清楚它們是如何移動 , 並搞清楚它們做了什麼事 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並且找出方法 , 正確地看待正在發生的事情 , 但是不是這麼真實 , 細胞中的小規模擠壓將會防止這種vista發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我現在要給你們看的是我們製作的這個影片的第一個版本 。 這是一個持續進行的企劃要花四到五年才完成 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這段影片 , 看到細胞製造這些會走路的小機械 , 它們叫做驅動蛋白 , 將巨大的負荷放大 , 以相對大小的單位來挑戰一隻螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請開始播放 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但是這些能驅動細胞內部的機械 , 真的很神奇 , 它們是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機械 , 彼此之間都存在著互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們導致細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅需要的零件 , 這些資訊是從細胞核中被讀取基因的分子所取得的 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , chris才會出席 , 真的很稀少 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex快遞小弟 ,
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他把一袋新蛋白放到細胞所需之處 , 不論是到細胞膜上 , 不論是用來製造或是修復某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人身上大約有十萬個這種細胞 , 運行著 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 在本質上 , 你其實什麼也不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 回家後 , 我希望你們能想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到的一些關於細胞機械的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚這些後 , 相信我 , 我們就能知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦知道發生了什麼事 , 我們將來真的能有大量的控制權 , 控制我們的健康 , 用我們後代子孫所做的 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能藉此發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們能意識到細胞需要它們做什麼來操作它們 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起努力 , 讓細胞完成它所需要的事情 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們合力使我們的身體產生巨大的實體 , 使得它們無法正常看見它們的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請繼續欣賞接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓在她的車上住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但是 , 當憂鬱裝成以及自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅行變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她在美國工作無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險 , 快樂 , 生命 , 個人成長 , 貧窮 , 社會變遷 , 社會和說故事等 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個超有好奇心的人 , 所以 , 身為記者 , 我學會了很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學懂的其中一件事就是當個隱世人
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後我決定去旅行
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的去世對我打擊很大 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事的時候 , 我有很多想要去感覺和處理的事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我這一生都在露營我決定在旅行車中生活一年就像一趟漫長的露營旅行
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包貓 , 我的洛威拿鐵還有我的露營裝備 , 穿上1975年雪佛蘭旅行車直開車去看日落完全沒有想到三件很關鍵的事
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會把住在一個永久的架構中 , 甚至是一座小屋 , 作為一個人 , 有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 這種其他人的負面看法很快會影響到我們的現實 , 假如我們容許的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車真的很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 我定期在外用餐
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間休息和哀悼悲痛
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親過世時的憤怒和沮喪開始了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	自由工作結束了 。 我必須找全職來支付帳單
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天卻轉變為炎熱的夏天
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	更明顯的我帶著一隻貓和狗到哪裡去了 , 到處都去停車 。 那真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗來回地跑
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗送到日間護理中心
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能夠使用辦公大樓和卡車站的員工淋浴設備 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共休息室洗身
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫下腐壞
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰粒 , 幾小時就融化了而且還蠻悲慘的
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找到一間公寓 , 或住不起能讓我擁有羅特威爾和貓的公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	而我拒絕放棄 , 所以我繼續住在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當夜間的高溫讓我連走五十英尺外的公共洗手間 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降至零度以下 , 牠們還待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我又面臨了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都把不同的地方停下來 , 避免被警察發現 , 並惹上麻煩 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不是每次都成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺失去了對我的生活的掌控 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成一個住在車裡的無家者 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒有變 , 我的智商沒有降低 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、正直、價值觀 , 所有關於我的事物 , 仍然保持不變 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我卻不知怎地改變了
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪的旋渦裡越鑽越深
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊裡任何人一樣都很臭、很沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或喝得高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家可歸的人發現 , 包括一個前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你本非無家 , 你為何落得如此下場 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不把我當成無家可歸者 , 但我有 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	那教授聽完我的故事後 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者是沒有希望的 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥物有一種反應 , 會讓我有憂鬱症 , 讓我有了自殺傾向 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺了 , 就沒人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅素 , 一位全國知名的記者 , 在全國廣播的電視節目上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	在他去世前一年 , 我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 寫於提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在做一個講稿表演節目 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆羅斯 , 《與傳媒會見》前主持tm竟然在談論我的寫作當時我住在旅行車裡的停車場裡卻開始大笑
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為它到達了我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那 , 重新讀一次自己的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是一個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	像是住在旅行車裡 , 和朋友在沙發上玩沙發 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又重新開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的夏天 , 我是個工作記者 ,
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我得了獎 。 我住進了我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數千人全職工作兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會卻持續汙名化並將住在車上或在街頭生活視為犯罪行為 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者、工作無家者 , 主要還是維持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們、鼓勵他們、給他們希望 ,
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的心靈可以克服一切事物 , 只要它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家者的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是想鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個乞討者 ,
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但 , 我來此告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 大家的住處和睡在哪裡 , 或是人生中的狀況是什麼 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪超市的停車場內而今天我卻在ted演講
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶領我們走過全國的大膽的計劃 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步 , 人口控制 。 這代表著許多法蘭克 , 搞笑的 , 以及非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaidya:如何保險套讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定針對此點下手 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 也不是減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從節育計畫著手 , 著手一個非常成功的婦女健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受節育計畫 , 如果孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:去找孩童 , 去找母親 , 然後再進行家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 1974年的確如此 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子 , 非常驚人的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們就說: 「 就去做吧 ! 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: " 我們也同意 , 我們會用避孕藥 , 但我們需要醫生來幫我們開藥 。 " 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不行 」 視為一種答案 ; 我們把 「 不行 」 視為一種問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看了護士和助產士 , 她也是女性 , 在解釋如何使用避孕藥方面 , 做得很棒 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但這只佔了全國20%的面積 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做些什麼 , 讓他們獨自一人 , 並說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你們所看到的那些普通人
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	在那黃色標牌下面 , 我希望他們沒有擦掉 , 因為那邊有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那個年代我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們所選的人是我們所選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們做得很棒 , 他們自己也會做節育計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應避孕藥和保險套 , 在全國各個村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就去了 。 我們去了那些被視為問題解決方案的成因的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論那裡有人 , 你可以看到船和婦女無處不在 , 都是漂浮市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有各種避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到人 , 你都能在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不找宗教家呢 ? 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會堅強 , 而泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在照片裡是穿藍色衣服的 , 不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在避孕藥和保險套上灑水 , 以保險套為神聖 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳遍全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧人自己也在做同樣的事情 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人都在說: " 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	原來是被賜福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們找上教師
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人去試著提供任何能讓人類變得更好的東西 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	有超過25萬人接受節育計畫 , 使用新的字母a、b出生、c代表保險套、子宮切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇與梯子遊戲 , 讓你投擲骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在有承諾的計劃之上 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如 「 媽媽每晚吃的藥丸
very good , mother . move ahead .	很好 , 媽媽 。 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	舅舅買保險套 。 非常好 , 舅舅 , 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	舅舅喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再開始 。 」

we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 該計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想要借錢給有執行節育計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 就照顧你的懷孕期 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡貸款 。 」

obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯的 , 他已經做切除手術了 , 因為他有一半的熱狗被吃掉了 , 而且他非常開心 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人民脫離貧窮 , 現在愛滋病脫離了困境 , 這次不是只靠政府 , 而是和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧困的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和借貸信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些要由商業界提供的東西
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試圖把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 一些小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法 , 就是透過企業 。
so , that was done .	這是完成的 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司的經費從村子透過樹木移植
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植了樹木 , 其金錢可以植入他們的小額貸款基金中 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入了 , 他們感覺自己擁有了銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在能借到錢之前 , 你需要受過訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用能力就必須是一項人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 必須要先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	下面我們稱之為赤腳企管碩士 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 就會成功經營這個生意 。

they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該不要再做鞋子和衣服了 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育上 , 我們想要改變學校的做法 , 讓這個學校的教學被沒用的地方 , 讓它成為每個人都一生的學習中心 。
