your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能會感覺像朋友 , 但真正的朋友 , 會偶爾微笑一下 。 在ted2013 , 凱勒琳娜杜介紹摩爾摩 , 智慧型手機的迷你機器人可以和你一起散步 , 在桌上滑動一杯咖啡 , 然後用可程式表達的表情對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	凱勒.瑞諾:一個迷你機器人靠你的手機供給你的手機動力 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉一下手 , 在座有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 其實這兩隻手 , 如果你不包括roombaba--你們當中有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們romotive公司試著去解決的問題我和其他20位知名人士都著迷於解題
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想造出一個人人都可以用的機器人不管你是八歲還是八十歲
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	事實證明 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要做出一個小而可攜帶式的機器人 , 它不但要能負擔得起 , 還必須要是大家真的想要帶家回家 , 並讓孩子圍繞的機器人 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能很詭異或不討喜 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要是友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 會用的是一種你已經知道且愛你的iphone , 來當作它的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量我們可以創造一個連接wifi無線網路的機器人同時擁有電腦視覺能力 , 只要150塊美金 , 這大約是過去這類機器人的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo被喚醒時 , 他正在生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上正在裝置上使用攝影機跟著我的臉
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我蹲下 , 他會跟著我
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很謹慎 , 所以他會把注意力放在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我從這邊過來 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我走到這邊他很聰明
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣感到害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--呃-哦 , romo累了--如果我想要和romo一起探索世界 , 我可以將他和任何ios的設備做連結 。
so here's the ipad .	所以這ipad就是
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	romo會將視訊串流到這個裝置 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	所以我可以看見romo看到的一切 , 然後我得到了一個機器人的視角世界 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這在appstore中是一個免費的應用程式 , 所以如果你們在手機上有這個應用程式 , 我們現在可以共同控制這個機器人 , 並一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我現在很快地給你們看romo實際上他是在串流影片所以你們可以看到我和整個ted觀眾
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我在這romo的前面
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我可以直接開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以我可以駕駛他到處走動 , 我可以幫你拍張照片 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要有張一千五百個ted觀眾的照片
so i'll snap a picture .	所以我拍了一張照片
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就跟你在ipad上滑動內容一樣 , 我可以在裝置上調整照相機的角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以你們所有人透過romo的眼睛
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo像是我的分身 , 我可以透過他的情緒來表達我自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去對romo說 , 讓我們來讓romo興奮一下 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的事是我們想要創造一個完全憑直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教他人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰會想去駕駛機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人處在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	他實際上是在任意兩個智慧型設備之間做雙向的音訊和影像串流 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	所以你可以透過瀏覽器來登入 , 它就像是有輪子的skype一樣 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們之前談到遠端臨場感 。 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	例如 , 你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 擁有iphone , 而她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 。 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能見到她孫女一兩次而已 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的幾個很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我最後想談談我們未來在努力的議題 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這實際上是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個稱為blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些代表各種程式碼的小方塊同時也創造任何你想要這個機器人所需要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式以創造romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這些行為 , 這就是你在左邊看到romo正在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中去執行它 , 在現實生活中執行該程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	接著 , 如果你有什麼值得讓你驕傲的你可以和世界上任何一個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些連接wifi無線網路的機器人 , 其實會互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們極度專注於建造一個大家都能訓練的機器人的原因是我們認為 , 在個人機器人領域中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式是個人 。
they change from person to person .	它們會因為人而改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	因此我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中放置一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己想像出來的具體實現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 這不是十年、一百億美金 , 也不是一個大型的類人型機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在現在 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像romo那樣 , 以及像你們這樣的人所創造的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及把機器人送到你們全部人的手上 , 我們也等不及要看看你們創造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和社會運動者伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 這場演講中也充滿激情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球性議題 , 愛情 , 養育子女 , 講故事 , 女性 , 世界文化 ,
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述激情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常感謝 。 站在這裡真是可怕 , 成為最聰明的人之一 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要跟大家說幾個熱情的故事
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人的說法是我很喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想傳達一些比事實更真誠的事 , 像是我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些甚至令我不安 , 直到最後我把它們寫下來 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治及社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的奧秘 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆感情、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但是過著匿名的生活 , 直到2006年2月當我在義大利舉行奧運時 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在人們意識到我在梅西百貨公司 , 我的孫子們都覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	請容許我在此告訴各位我出名的四分鐘
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話通知我獲選成為護旗者之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這一定是認錯人了因為我根本不是運動員
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定可走得完體育場一圈要是不用助步器
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是開玩笑
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是第一次只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性將分別代表五大洲另外還有三位奧運金牌得主
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說一套制服 , 要求我量測 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一幅景象可以穿著鬆軟的大動脈 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中旬 , 我到了杜林 , 人群充滿熱情在街上 , 歡呼參加奧運的80支隊伍 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了一切去競爭比賽 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有好運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的小東西 , 冰的一英吋 , 風的力量 , 可以判斷出種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 ,
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報上面印著奧運標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	激情就在這裡 。 不就是一直都是這樣嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心 , 是我們的動力 , 決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要充滿反對意見、反對者、冒險者、外人和反抗者 , 他們會問問題、打破規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	常識的好人不會創造有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會是好前夫
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我見到其他護旗手三位運動員、演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女性來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主旺加里•馬塔伊這些人種植了三千萬棵樹他們藉此改善了土壤和天氣當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨行動派女子蘇曼麗•曼她熱忱地對抗兒童妓女
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 祖父將她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴這些人相信跟年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	還有那些逼孩子們每天接客515次的妓院如果孩子反抗 , 就會被電擊折磨
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	不是我平常穿的服裝 , 但那件跟我原本想穿的米其林男人裝很遠 , 其實還不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但是 , 其他護旗手也一樣 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭這個世界公認的美麗與熱情的象徵
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她性感、纖瘦又高 , 身上有著很深的油脂 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 如何才能有一輛深色的棕色 , 沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當被問到 「 她怎麼可以這麼好看 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直的 , 我也不會發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你有來自地球上最美麗女人之一的一些免費的建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不吼、咳嗽、氣喘不自言自語、不放屁
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒說錯 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在大約午夜的時候 , 我們被叫到體育場的翅膀 , 擴音機傳來了奧運國旗 , 順便說一句 , 音樂的開始是和這裡的音樂相同 , aida遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英呎 , 不算一頭很粗的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子的一角舉在肩上 。 我則在後面小跑步追還在手上握著旗子所以我的頭其實在那面該死的旗子下面
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的鏡頭當然是蘇菲雅
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在大多數刊出的照片中 , 雖然常是出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個多數男人都很想去的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的4分鐘就是那些在奧運體育館
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公聽我這麼說時我覺得被冒犯了即使我跟他解釋 , 我們私下作的事通常撐不到4分鐘所以他不應該親自去做
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有那4分鐘不可思議的剪輯 , 因為我不想忘記在我老的時候 , 發生腦細胞損傷 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我希望永遠將奧運的關鍵字放在心中
so here's a tale of passion .	所以這是一個充滿熱情的故事
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點是一座囚營 , 營區是剛果境內的圖西族難民 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	對了 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是婦女和女童 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是個年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子們
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 是個寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她眼睜睜看著自己的丈夫被凌虐至死 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她竟然讓她7個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子自己割斷臍帶然後用頭髮把斷口綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的名字為雙胞胎命名以取得他們的青睞 , 並用黑色茶餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法支撐他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	軍人們闖進她的牢房要強暴她大女兒時她抓著女兒不放手即便頭上抵著槍
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這家人存活了16個月 , 然後 , 靠著絕佳的運氣 , 和一個年輕男子沙夏•查諾夫的熱情 , 讓她能夠進入美國救援機 , 蘿絲•瑪班多和她的9個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 他們現在都在那居住和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且富熱情的女性就像蘿絲•瑪班多
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不是編造它們的 , 不需要它們 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都可看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性一起工作 ,
i know them well .	我對他們很熟 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 世界末日 , 在父系的天主教及保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我5歲就已經是個熱血沸騰的女權主義者儘管當時我還未到過智利所以沒人知道我到底是哪根筋不對勁
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	很快地 , 我就會發現要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 還要去質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但是我很高興能夠付出代價 , 因為每當我受到的一擊 , 我就能夠提供兩支 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會 , 我應該接著走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們還有一場令人難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒和在座各位這樣幸福的女性 , 是的 , 但對其他國家大部分的姊妹們來說 , 她們仍然被逼著過早結婚、賣淫、被迫勞動 , 她們有不想要或無法餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時因為受罰被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對今天大部分西方女性來說 , 被稱為女權主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權從來就不吸引人 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我很少有缺乏男性的情感 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權還未死 , 絕非如此 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的緣故 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	改叫愛芙若蒂、維納斯或金寶 , 隨便你想 , 名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它的意義 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以這是另一個有熱情的故事 , 這是個令人難過的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉一個村莊的小婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國潔牙師她到診所當義工奉獻自己3星期的假期
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要潔淨牙了 , 但她到了那裡之後 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是個充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排排已經等了好幾個小時的女性受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當因為她有好幾顆臼齒
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的辦法就是拔掉壞牙
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 也從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她很常冒險 , 很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的工具還好帶了一些麻醉藥
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢而熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她喃喃祈禱 , 然後開始拔牙
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後病患吻了她的手
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生人員拔了更多的牙齒
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次到達所謂的診所時她的第一個病人和丈夫一起等她
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	那女人的臉看起來像西瓜
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣憤 , 威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被自己造成的後果嚇壞了但是翻譯解釋病人的狀況跟手術無關
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打敗她 , 因為她不在家裡準備晚餐 , 要為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬女性過著這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	縱使女性分擔世界上3分之2的勞力工作卻僅擁有不到1%的全球資產
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	同一份工作的薪資卻低於男性 , 如果他們的薪水完全沒有 , 且他們仍然是脆弱的 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且不斷受到開發、暴力及虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實就是提供女性教育、工作掌管自己收入的能力、繼承並擁有財產 , 對社會有益
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女人有力量 , 她的孩子和家人就會過得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家戶繁榮起來 , 村落也會繁榮 , 最終整個國家也會繁榮 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人們談話並解釋土地已經貧瘠因為砍樹賣掉了
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女人們種植新的樹一滴接著一滴
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在短短五或六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤富含土壤 , 拯救了整個村莊 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮最落後的社會總是把女性放下來的
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而這顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性相關計畫每得到1美元就有20美元用來資助男性相關計畫
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類總數的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予她們力量將改變一切不僅是科技、設計和娛樂
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證 , 要是女性合作串聯、有知識並受教育就能為這個病入膏板的星球帶來和平與繁榮
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷最多的都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 死傷都是附帶損害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人掌管世界 , 看看我們所擁有的一團糟 ,
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要怎樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們要一個保存生命的世界一個生活品質能夠均富非僅限幸運群體的地方
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份 , 我看了費南多•巴特羅的畫展在博克萊大學圖書館
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有任何博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊外 , 搬運巴特羅的作品 , 膽敢展示這幅畫 , 因為題材是發生虐囚案的阿布格雷布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是虐待和權力暴力的大幅畫作大量的用巴特羅風格呈現
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把那些圖像從我的腦海或心中得到 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無能為力的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力以及濫用權力
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並逼迫其他成員接受這個現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在變 , 但總有益處 , 在這種情況下 , 下滲效應 , 在經濟學上行不通的 , 效果相當好 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	把濫用手法從梯子的頂端到最底端 ,
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 特別是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最一無所有的男人也有人可以虐待一個女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數通過性別、收入、種族和階級的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以對我們的文明做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們就需要女性化的能量 , 管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要讓一群很關鍵的女性 , 在有權力的位置上 , 我們需要培養男性心中的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我說的是有年輕心智的男人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙沒什麼希望 , 我們要等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和著名的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但若能選擇 , 我寧願有顆勇敢的心像汪佳•瑪太、蘇曼麗•媽媽、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界
not better , but to make it good .	還不是比較好 , 而是要讓它變好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是可能的 。 看看四周--這些知識、活力、才華和科技
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們離開扇子 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在一個和倫敦一樣大的城市中 , 共有三千萬份餐 , 可是所有的食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡林鋼鐵討論了日常瑣事的奇蹟:供應一座城市的食物路線如何形塑現代化世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynseel:食物如何形塑我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為 , 如果我們去一家商店或餐廳 , 或一小時之內進到戲院大廳 , 就會有食物等著我們神奇地出現 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到倫敦這麽大的城市每天有足夠的食物被製造運輸、買、賣煮、吃、處置同樣的事 , 日復一日發生在每個城市裏 , 每個城市都要有足夠的食物 , 這點是相當了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 好像牠們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了我們也是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 實際上我們和古老的祖先一樣也依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們愈來愈多進入城市 , 更多那種自然世界的景觀 , 被改造成像我身後的景觀 。 這是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 目的是餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景色十分特別 , 但少有人見識過 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而且越來越多的這些景觀並不只是用來餵飽我們
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們愈來愈多進入城市 , 更多人開始吃肉 , 這麼一來 , 全球每年的穀物中 , 有三分之一都被餵食動物 , 而不是被我們人類食用 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	要消耗三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物如果用在動物身上的話首先通過的話這是效率不高的養育方式
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個越來越嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們住在城市的人數會是現在的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	估計也將多吃兩倍的肉和乳製品
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和都市主義手上都提升了 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們還像現在一樣繼續下去 , 那將會是一個我們非常不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 創造出新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去相當於現存的可耕地因爲土地的鹽化和水土流失
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也非常渴求 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	在西方每製造一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的能量
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即使有我們用大量成本生產的食物 , 我們事實上並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	目前美國有半數生產的食物被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這個漫長的過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有管理適當的餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	有十億人過胖 , 卻也有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	一點都不合理
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球百分之八十的食物交易只由五大跨國企業所掌控這是一個嚴峻的圖片
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬到城市裡時 , 同時也接受了西方的飲食習慣 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們展望未來 , 不穩定的飲食
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼辦 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	為了回答稍微容易一些的問題 , 大約在一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開始 , 在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的新月沃土 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是新月的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明農業及城市主義大約在同一地點同一時間發生了
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市是息息相關的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們遠古祖先首度發現的穀物 , 足以生產足夠大的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久定居 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些定居處 , 我們會發現它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們的周圍有農田並以一大型神殿為中心例如這一個在烏爾的神殿在當時是神聖化的中央食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排農作收割收集穀物獻給諸神再把諸神沒吃的穀物發還給人們
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的所有精神及實體生活都是由他們賴以維生的穀物和收成所主宰 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 這對每一個古老城市來說都是如此
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元一世紀時 , 羅馬有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以像這樣的城市如何養活自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬靠近海所以食物可以從很遠的地方運來
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是古代唯一可行的方法 , 因為要運送食物到道路上是非常困難的 , 差不多就是這樣 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	而且食物很快就壞掉 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地在爲了取得他們的穀物存量保留區而引發戰爭而引發戰 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說這個帝國的擴張真的很長一段時間以後才會有軍事化的購物中心
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬還曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段我覺得這很了不起 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬用它的食欲來塑造它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 其他事情也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	看看17世紀的倫敦地圖我們可以發現 , 穀物是從泰晤士河運入在這張圖的下方
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場位於城市的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路上從他們帶領的道路到廉價的地方 , 也就是主要市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你細看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你就能知道300年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	想當然爾對魚也是如此
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然是從河裡捕到的 。 同樣地 ,
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	比林斯門是過去倫敦有名的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的很特別 , 真的 , 想想看
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人手上都有一支手機 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點臭的魚正從港口下來 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事 。 一旦進入城市的根部就被建立起來了 , 它們就幾乎不會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類產品則是另外一回事因為 , 動物們當然能走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北城 。 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 所在的位置 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞來到東北方
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得自己有點像氣象女子在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類的進來就是靠著帆布保護鞋進入 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當牠們抵達區普塞得東邊時 , 就是牠們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼我們稱之為 「 家禽區 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你去看任一城市的地圖在工業時代前你可以追溯食物的來源
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	真的可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 。 無論是通過閱讀街道的名字 , 讓你可以得到很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也得要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街上和公共空間是買賣食物唯一的場所
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫像你可以看到這樣的城市很難不注意你的食物從哪裡來
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜日午餐 , 吃的東西可能性很大 , 可能是三天前在你的窗外吹氣或在你的窗外大呼吸 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 是一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	而十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的景象 ,
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你可以看到 , 最早的鐵路旅客中有一些是豬和羊
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	牠們在眼不見心為淨的情況下被屠宰在鄉下的某處
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並且藉由鐵路運進城市
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	一開始 , 它是有史以來第一次能在任何地方 , 培養出任何大小和形狀的城市 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去 , 它們得要透過非常困難的實體方式來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理學中被解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從倫敦的地圖上可以看出在火車通行的90年後倫敦從一個容易餵飽的小點一個靠動物走進來就能餵飽的小點到一個龐然大物化的地點很難餵飽任何人無論是動物或是人
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然那只是個開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車這成就了這個過程的終點
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放徹底地從大自然的任何明顯關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這是城市中沒有氣味、沒有混亂、沒有人居住 , 因為本來根本沒人會夢想要走在這種景色中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們拿到食物的做法是他們上車 , 開車到郊區的某一處 , 帶著一星期的購物回來 , 然後好奇這玩意兒要拿這玩意兒怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	就在這個時刻 , 我們與食物及城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	在這裡 , 我們有過去食物是中心 , 是城市的社會核心 , 在邊緣區域 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社會活動的一部分 , 買賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們曾要料理食物 , 現在只需要加水 , 或加點蛋 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不聞東西的味道 , 看看是否有東西吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需要讀包裝背後的標籤
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不珍惜食物 , 也不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是珍視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代飲食習慣最諷刺的就是他們把他們所承諾的非常好的部分弄得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由在任何地方、任何地方建造城市 , 他們其實讓我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 也就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	他們也讓我們依賴只有他們能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾就在問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他著作《烏托邦》這本書的前影
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	而且那是一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 如果聽起來有點熟悉 , 有一天走在彼此的道路上 , 人人基本上都是農田 , 在後花園種植蔬菜 , 然後一起吃一頓共用餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的根本原則即便是更多的原則都不曾如此看待
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個著名的烏托邦的願景:艾貝納•霍華著的 " 花園城市 "
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 一些小型的都會區 , 周圍有農田圍繞 , 透過鐵路連接彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	食物可以被說是他視覺的原理 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至已經建好 , 但與霍華的願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦理念的問題所在 , 它們是烏托邦的
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	" 烏托邦 " 是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意選用的詞
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有希臘語中的雙重含義 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以指一個好地方 , 或一個沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的、想像的 , 我們無法擁有
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 做為一種概念性工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深刻問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了另一種辦法 , 像是希托邦 , 從古希臘文 「 sitos 」 , 意思是 「 topos 」 , 一個地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在 " 希托邦 " 裏
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到這一點 , 我們就可以把食物當作是強而有力的工具──一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式來塑造這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這麼做 , 希托邦可能會長得怎樣 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 , 只是狗臉上的表情
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	無論如何 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享用 , 人們會花時間在這件事上 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物在我們社會的位置 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	對了 , 這些也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	就是那些會想到食物的人 , 會預先思考 , 作計劃 , 可以盯著一堆生菜的一群人 , 實際認出他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一份子
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就無法擁有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	我故意選這張是因為這是男人在買菜
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是 「 網絡 」 、 「 食物是當地生長 」 的市場 ,
it's common . it's fresh .	是普遍的 , 新鮮的
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為這個城市社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這一部分 , 就不可能有這種地方 , 本地種植的食物也是景觀的一部分 , 不僅僅是零和商品在看不見的地獄裡生長 。
cows with a view .	牛群帶有一種觀點
steaming piles of humus .	冒著水汽的肥沃土壤
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上這就是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是一個社區性的計劃我最近去了一趟多倫多
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	那是溫室 , 孩子們能告訴所有的食物 , 種自己食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫凱文的植物 , 或許它是屬於凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類計畫正試圖將我們和大自然再度連繫在一起是非常重要的
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到希托邦已經在小口袋裡存在 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	秘訣在於要把它們結合起來 , 用食物作為一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這麼做 , 我們就不會再把城市看成一個大型的、不生產性的區塊 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 把它們看成是有機架構的一部分 , 無可避免地連接在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但 , 當然 , 那也不是什麼好形象 , 因為我們得要再也不用做這樣的食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多想想永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖替我做個總結 , 我們需要做的思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種對於食物塑造我們生活的方式的重新概念 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是650年前拍的 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是安布羅吉歐.羅倫澤提的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	和城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事情的訊息非常清楚
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市細心照顧國家 , 這國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我希望我們現在去問安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤提會怎麼畫 ? 如果他今天畫這張圖 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天 , 好的政府的寓言該長什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到世界是我們所吃下的食物 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們能把食物當作真正有力的工具來改善世界
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	《慈悲憲章》的幾週後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯檢視了宗教在21世紀扮演的角色:它的教條會分我們嗎 ? 還是它會團結我們 , 是因為它有共同的利益 ? 她會檢視推動世界對於黃金法則的催化劑
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal9、2009年的暴力、暴力、
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重溫黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為 , 身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心的核心 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都進化出他們自己的版本被稱為黃金法則
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它也有正面的版本: 「 總是把所有其他人當作是別人看待的自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 己所不欲 , 勿施於人 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	直視自己的內心 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 接著在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下都拒絕將那種痛苦加諸於任何人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調的是同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它很好聽 , 而是因為它很有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則就像孔子的說: 「 不論每天 」 一整天 , 都只是想著做好事 , 然後又回到貪婪且自私的生活中 。 但是如果持續不懈地實行 , 你就會把自己從世界的中心推下 , 換到另一個你 , 然後你超越自我 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會引領你到一個名為 「 神 」 的境界 。 奇蹟、回教、寶塔 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	一些超越我們所知的超越了我們在有限的存在之上
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活來說實在太重要了 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖會團結在一起 , 他們會爭論深奧的教義 , 或說是仇恨的議會 , 或者反對同性戀這一類的事 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	人們通常不太願意憐憫 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士交談時 , 看到他們的表情有一種互相衝突的表情 , 因為人們通常都希望自己是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	那我為什麼對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地帶領我離開我的書架研究 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我可以在更為廣大的觀眾面前演說 , 這遠超乎我的想像 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這件事非常急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實行黃金法則 , 這樣我們對待所有的人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們是誰 , 都一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 可以把這個世界交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 這個時代的偉大任務之一 , 是要建立一個全球化的社會 , 如同我之前說過的 , 讓人們能和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 相信黃金法則的人不只是虔誠的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種同理心的想像行為 , 把自己放在他人的處境中 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調自己的信仰 , 或者不寬容的一面 , 或者 , 我們可以回到比耶穌更久遠的猶太長老西勒爾 , 當一位異教徒在單腳站立時 , 他要一個猶太教徒來總結整個猶太教義 , 他說: 「 你不願為你的鄰居做同樣的事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是教義 , 其他都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	猶太教各長老以及早期教父說任何對經文的解讀只要培養出仇恨和輕視是非法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們必須復興這樣的精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	不僅僅因為愛的精神喚醒我們而發生 ,
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這個理想實現 , 我們可以通過ted所介紹的現代傳播溝通 ,
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經為我們所有伴侶的回應感到無比振奮 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一組人準備用《慈悲憲章》拯救新加坡社會最近出現的分歧 。 議會的某些成員也希望可以將憲章提升到政治層面 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 準備辦一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們看到 , 慈悲其實也是一切藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 各個穆斯林社群舉辦了許多活動和討論 , 討論以悲憫為中心的思想在伊斯蘭教以及所有信仰的核心問題 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就這樣停住 。 它不能就這樣停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教誨 , 這就是我們出錯的地方 , 完全只聚焦在相信深奧的教義上 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨應該要付諸行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	而我打算在這起我死去的日子裡努力
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 去教育和激發慈悲的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們太過放棄慈悲
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常覺得這只對某人感到抱歉
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但是 , 如果你只是這樣想 , 你當然不理解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你還得去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體能夠參與其中 , 因為媒體的重要性在於要幫忙分解我們對其他人的一些刻板印象觀點 , 這些觀點將我們彼此區隔開來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也同樣適用
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能夠感受到動力 , 動力與挑戰一種以仁愛的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它要求急性智商 , 而不僅僅是一時的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想請學者一起來探索他們自己的同情心及他們傳統中的同情心 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 鼓勵那些不寬容的演講不為人知的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們都有這個憲章 , 不管他們的信仰為何 , 或缺乏他們自己的信仰 , 他們覺得有能力去挑戰那些不熱情的言論 , 那些鄙視的言論來自他們的宗教領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業界的首領 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過憲章可以放上網路 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 有一大堆棺材坐在房間裡 , 發出又一條神秘的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted為我提供了一種全新的方式來思考和發表構想 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這正是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識如果我們聯手合作我們就有可能改變世界
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有時候問題似乎也讓人無法解決 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但是我要引用最後的一段話來引用一位英國作家 , 牛津學者的話我不太常提到他 , c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話一直在我腦中揮之不去 , 打從我讀書開始 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四種愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨了愛欲 , 當兩個人凝視對方的眼睛時 , 會拼寫下去 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這種感情與友情比較 , 兩個人肩並肩 , 眼中固定著一個共同目標 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我非常強烈的感受到 , 在我們維多利亞小小的警告期間 , 當不同說服的人聚在一起 , 肩並肩努力朝著共同的目標前進 , 差異就會消失 。
and we learn amity .	而我們會學習到的是雄心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 學會認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay重新審視這次的勝利 , 有時甚至超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬主義者完成的羅馬主義者邁進 , 他對於歷史城市的致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgrant , 藝術 , 藝術 , 書籍 , 城市 , 交流 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事 。

sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我畫了很多卻還是不明白我在畫什麼
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	在座如果有數位產品可以自在 , 甚至在網路上走走 , 會覺得有趣 , 知道以 「 事物運作 」 為名的那個人 , 做好一部分 「 理解 」 這件事 , 花兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆電和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直在管理自己的延伸 , 以致於我從來沒有意識到閱讀指示 。 但我終於明白了 。 我必須弄清楚 , 因為接到邀請時 , 提醒我們 , 沒有投影機 , 所以把那些卡車帶過來 , 沒有必要 , 只是一些另類的溝通方式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我的成名作品 , 它會特別適合在場的許多技術性思維的人 , 或是我可以談談我真正關心的事情 。

well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在羅德島設計學院念建築的時候 , 是在六零年代後期 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 在我當學生的最後一年 , 也就是第五年 , 在羅馬度過 。 這改變了我的一生 。

so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我就會試著在裡面做些什麼 , 或用它或為了它做些什麼 。

the primary reason for all these dead ends is when if you're not quite sure where you're going , you're certainly not going to get there with any kind of efficiency .	所有死路一條的主要原因是如果你不太確定到底要去哪裡 , 你絕對不會有任何效率 。
here's a little map . and i thought of maps at the beginning ; maybe i should just try and do a little atlas of my favorite streets and connections in rome .	這裡有一張小地圖 。 我一開始就想到了地圖 , 或許我應該畫一張小地圖 , 上面是羅馬最愛的街道和連線圖 。

maybe i should get away from this map completely , and really be honest about wanting to show you my favorite bits and pieces of rome and simply kick a soccer ball in the air which happens in so many of the squares in the city and let it bounce off of things . and i'll simply explain what each of those things is that the soccer ball hits .	也許我該跳脫繪製地圖坦誠地展示我偏愛羅馬地哪些部分就這麽踢一腳球就像在城市裡的很多廣場上讓它彈來彈去 。 我來解釋球彈到的各個點 。

so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	於是我們進入了萬神殿內部 , 它會成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我走對路了 , 但那有點失去了人性的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想吸引別人把注意力放在一本書上 , 一路上收集資訊 , 那永遠是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	" 鴿子的進展 " 令我驚訝的頭銜
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是一隻回家的鴿子那就會叫做《荷馬的奧德修紀》
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題能用它 。 但它會是一趟旅程 , 穿越羅馬 , 展示所有我喜愛的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子正坐在教堂頂上
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天飛走 , 做做正常的鴿子該做的事 , 再飛回來 , 整個地方都佈滿支架和綠色防護網 , 這只鴿子不可能飛回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須找到另一個棲身之處 , 這讓我能夠通過我最喜歡的目錄 , 我們從最高的那些開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人生活在一起 ; 這樣不一定是好事 , 但牠確實可以再次將鴿子凝聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我在想 , 這有點意思可是應該有個人也來參與一下
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想到了一個老傢伙 , 他終其一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方去救他們危險的地方之類的 , 他們會和這個人變成朋友 , 在午餐時間和他玩耍的時候學會了把戲給他玩 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老男人和這些鴿子之間發展出真正的鍵結
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但很不幸的他生病了 , 病的很重
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導了他們拼他的名字aldo
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天沒見到他之後 , 有一天他住在這個小閣樓裡 , 他們把他的名字拼寫在身邊 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一支紅氣球 , 在一旁等著他 , 然後他們帶著他 , 飛過城牆 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城墻外面去 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死者從未被埋藏在城牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個讓人高興的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	不管怎麼說 , 我還是去看了再一次 , 如果包裝沒有成功 , 如果故事沒成功 , 我只是想出了書名 , 希望書名可以把我往對的方向踢開 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它的確讓我非常專注 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些書名最後引領我找到了我定居的解決方案 , 這故事是一位年輕女子傳了一則信息給家鄉的鴿子她住在羅馬城外的城牆上對著羅馬人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從阿庇安公路上飛下來 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到古墓、松柏和其它的林林總 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看見那條紅線 , 你就可以看到鴿子的行蹤如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時就變得有必要又可行 , 試著傳達這種感覺 , 無需實際移動就能飛越城市 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--這些對你來說可能很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬渡海門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件其它鴿子歸巢時不做的事:它選擇了一條觀光路線 , 這個設備是我覺得這本書需要超越四頁的範圍 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	於是我們環繞羅馬競技場一周 , 飛過希臘聖母教堂 , 和海克力士的神殿 , 向河流靠近 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	差點撞上法尼斯古拉索夫斯的飛利尼斯 , 由米開朗基羅設計 , 由羅馬競技場拆下來的石頭建成 ,
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰campode小屋
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事因為這是完全雜亂的一種完全不依規則化的看法 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法就是只要看上去可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你會試著找出消失點在哪 ; 有幾個就在火星上 , 還有別的幾個在克雷莫納 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但是進入廣場 , 就在和平聖母堂前面 , 在那裡 , 永遠都有一場足球比賽正在進行 , 而我們卻被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這張圖說明了被足球擊中是很糟糕的狀況 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我畫上了它的各個部分 。 和平聖母堂 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀的一小部分 。 我不得不重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看清楚很平聖母堂--像這樣的書很靈活 , 很互動--只要把它掉個個個 , 從另一面看
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到撞擊發生在紅線上
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鴿子在中世紀的塔樓上空調整了過來--其中一個中世紀剩下的中世紀塔樓了--向著san'agnese教堂附近的圓頂靠近我們已經向下俯瞰那廣場的圓頂我們已經看過和流過好幾次了 。 這是伯尼的雕像 , 上面是四條河流 , 然後經過了非常美妙的聖依華堂 。 在26英尺的天孔上停下來休息一下 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在不斷移動的同時 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用真的在這個特定的時刻擔心重力 , 所以這張圖能以任何方式朝向的方向前進 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	飛過gesu時我們會變得有些刺激--這樣算是不意外地模仿這個建築
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過這面牆 , 充斥著我所說的混合體 ; 漂亮的雕刻 , 沿著尼龍上方的 「 崛起人 」 標誌 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到了palazzo的前庭也就是目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人正在畫板上畫畫 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	牠把訊息從鳥的腿上移開 ; 牠是這樣說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	我們看看畫板上 , 看到他正在製作的其實是鴿子飛行的旅程地圖 , 紅線穿過所有畫面 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 所以我們完成這個循環的了解 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員 , 研究的是自行組合的基礎設備 , 我們不但能夠創造出可以自行組合的材料 , 更像是一股dna自行拼合的材料 。 在初期 , 這是個很大的概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三種印記 , 它暗示著一個自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天行的tibbits:我們能製造出本身的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 不久後 , 我們的建築物和機器將會自組 , 複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要告訴你我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後拿來和一些自然生態系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分組成 , 相當複雜 , 有令人振奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵 , 水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空--250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或dna有30億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且它們可以修復自己持續長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有個超級有趣之處 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那麼便會有一些令人興奮的潛力為我們建造物品的方式 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要利用我們的物理環境中的自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 讓我們的建築物和機器都能辦到 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列--基本上是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以使用該序列來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源將允許激活 , 讓我們的部分可以折疊程序 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的糾錯冗餘 , 以保證我們已經成功地建構我們所希望的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	接下來我會向各位展示一些項目 , 這些項目是我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自組的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前面的兩個是macrobot和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大型的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入機電設備 , 傳感器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你想要解碼什麼便折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 。 這樣的角度 , 或輪流順序 , 你便發送通過弦的序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120 , 它會旋轉到那裏 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 參與這個項目
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想它真的能引出光線:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 大量的人類時光完成這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人裝進每一個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著眼於被動的本質 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 嘗試以實際式計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最根本的計算 , 數位邏輯 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nand邏輯閘
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 它是門 , 它會做你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自用戶的輸入 , 如同你在做你的磚 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從以前被放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會讓你在三維空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著用戶可以開始插電他們想要做的磚塊
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它是之前做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它已經開始在三維空間裡移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左側 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 它便下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它便上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這就意味著 , 我們現在的結構包含了我們所要建設的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的構建信息嵌入其中
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我把它稱為自導複製 , 因為你的結構包含精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果有錯誤 , 可以更換部件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	因此 , 你可以擁有攀登的東西將它讀取 , 並在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目被稱為偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要的可重構性和可編程性 , 並使它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一個元素鏈 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 而且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一條鏈 , 或每個元素 , 想要右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這種情況下 , 一個螺旋 , 或者這個例子 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編程任何立體形狀--一維 , 二維--完全被動地進入這條產業鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來的資訊 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 這告訴了我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的新可能性在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器上 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們就會有空間的計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 橋樑 , 機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	因此 , 這有讓人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛才所展示的這些計畫 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們能實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界做準備 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登陸了月球 , 繪製了大陸地圖我們甚至到達了海底最深的地點 。 下一代還能探索什麼 ? 生物學家和探索家納粹沃爾夫斯提出了這個答案:幾乎所有一切都可以了 。 然後我們開始了 , 他說 , 在這無可避免的小世界中 , 可以說是 ,
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nthanwolfe:還有什麼好探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我是去那裡榮耀一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	當他在美國自然歷史博物館工作時 , andrews率領一系列到地圖上未標明地區的探險活動 , 像是這裏的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個不錯的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他之後成為印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
