and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表公眾演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在此告訴各位 , 如果有任何事情比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要在45分鐘的講座上保持一千個12歲孩子的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個自此之後深陷在我腦海中 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了一個問題: 「 我們應該要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為我們之中有很多人認為偉大的地球探索年代已經結束 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空還是最深的海洋 , 去尋找重要的可探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有剩下的重要地方可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想到生物學歷史中我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未被看見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是取出菸草屬植物的受感染汁液 , 用愈來愈小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他覺得一定有什麼東西是比當時所知的最微小型態的生命體小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人取了一個名字
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之病毒--源自拉丁文中的 「 毒藥 」
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , 實際上beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式生命的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實務應用和這個世界相關--像是天花的滅絕 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 而我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	beijerinck在一百多年前發現病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們已經有了汽車 , 但我們還不知道組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們能夠探索未知的世界──像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做得比只看到表面還要多 , 還能研究特定物種的個體基因組 , 還要研究整個萬個元組 , 包含將微生物的群體 , 存在我們周圍 , 並紀錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚間的所有物體上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在經常這樣做 , 來找出不明確造成疾病的爆發原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	讓各位了解一下這如何運作想像我們取了你們每一個人的鼻腔標本
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會做的 , 就是尋找呼吸道疾病如流行性感冒的病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始觀察基因信息 , 我們會看到一些普通的可疑物--當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒訊息 , 大部分都來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常、非常驚人的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這個信息時 , 我們會發現 , 在你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息 , 與我們以前見過的任何東西不吻合:植物、動物、菌類、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際在研究這種資料的小團體 , 其實我們當中有些人開始稱這個資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們見過的東西 , 它就像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的資訊都是暗物質 , 無法跟我們見過的任何東西歸類或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為或許這是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對很新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這信息是一種生命型態 , 或者至少當中有部分是有生命的 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都還在初步階段 , 但有個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那就是埋藏在生命的遺傳信息中 , 存在著許多未被辨識出生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們在探索一連串的a、t、c和g事物時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命種類 , 就像beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的認知 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許能讓我們找出折磨我們癌症的原因 , 或辨識我們不熟悉的爆發病症原因 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興的宣布 , 加上史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 我們正開始要探索生物暗物質 , 以尋求新種類生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 一種組成我們地球上大多數基因信息的生命型態 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚嘆於我們可能完全沒有察覺到在我們眼前的一個新生命類別 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們也可能發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的事物 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類為下一代的探險家提供了重要的一課--就像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們把這個教訓說出來 , 像這樣:不要假設我們目前認為存在的就是全部 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何一個你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	未知存在於我們周遭 , 它們等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch將背後的理論物理物理學討論更迫切的問題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷 , 宇宙 , 文化 , 環境 , 全球議題物理 , 科學 , 科技 , 宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要截肢時 , 說出驚人的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	而第一個 , 事實上 , 是有史以來最早就有過的歷史 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 太陽系 , 環境等獨特的特性 , 可以持續我們的演化或創造 , 就像過去的思想和現在的存在一樣 。 最重要的是 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇化的名字: 「 地球號太空船 」 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	有這樣的想法是在太空船的外面 , 宇宙是不可調和的充滿敵意 , 而其內部是我們賴以為生的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們弄砸我們的太空船 , 我們沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都已經知道的事是與人類歷史大部分時間所堅信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	就如史蒂芬•霍金說過我們只是存在於典型的星球表面的化學汙垢這個典型的星球在軌道上環繞著一個典型的恆星 , 位於一個典型的銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推.
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的兩件事當中的第一件大概是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合度等等 。 第二件是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你把這兩項當作生命中深刻的真理並以此作為你人生決策的依據 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩個是完全錯誤的
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 。 這是典型的 。 嗯 , 這也是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們看看四周 , 往一個隨機的方向看 , 我們看到了牆壁 , 化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝著同一個方向走數百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你將不會看到任何牆或著化學污垢 , 你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 星星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這在宇宙中仍然不算典型.因為恆星存在於星系中.
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 在任何星系都不存在 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們走出星系 , 然後再往回看 , 沒錯 , 有一個巨大的星系 , 螺旋臂停在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	到這個時候 , 我們已經有十萬光年的光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們離宇宙中一個典型的地方還很近 ,
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達典型的地方 , 你必須要跨銀河間的空間一千倍 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在這巨大開銷上 , ted用高解析度的方式呈現了星系間空間的虛擬世界--星系間空間的景觀.
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 我們可以看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	不是非常完美--在星系間的空間裡 , 非常的黑暗 , 非常的暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你在看離你最近的恆星時 , 那個恆星正被爆炸成超新星 , 當光線抵達你的時候 , 你甚至看不到任何閃光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是如此的巨大、黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管一個超新星這麼明亮 , 這麼傑出的事件 , 它還是會讓你在幾光年的範圍內被砸死 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但是在星系間空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你根本不會看見它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷不超過絕對零度三度.
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而它是非常空的 。 真空--密度比我們目前所能創造的最佳科技的真空濃度低了一百萬倍 。 所以這就是典型的地方是從這個地方來的 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是我們現在所處的典型狀況 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請開燈 , 謝謝.
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何得知一個離我們如此遙遠的環境 , 而如此不同 , 和陌生的環境 , 從我們習以為常的事物中知道 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球我們的環境 , 以我們的方式來創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這代表什麼呢 ? 看看比我們剛剛更遠--我是指以望遠鏡來看 , 你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們叫做類星體.類星體原意是指類星體.
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 離我們還有數十億光年之遠 , 星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量黑洞瓦解 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	隨後密集的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用.其中一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式回到外面去 , 照亮了它.而我認為它只是一個萬億個太陽的光亮.
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人腦的物理學大不像這種噴射流束的物理
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即生存 。 語言能當作描述噴射流中的情況時 , 就會瞬間分解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這可能有點像經歷一次超新星爆炸 , 但在零距離之下且持續了數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射流發生得如此地精確 , 以至於數十億年後在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是有你用來描述實際正在發生的事情 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個同類的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是個表面的圖像 , 雖然也包含在內 , 還有一個解釋性的模型 , 呈現出相同的數學關係和因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠神奇 , 另外一個結構的信念和時間的增長了 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這樣特別的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 儘管它們可能不同 , 仍然能體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間 , 能做得越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一種與眾不同的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢擁有普遍存在的通用性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構精準度不斷地提高 , 即 " 一切 " 的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 正是這個中心 , 包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果關係 。 此外 , 物理的規律允許這一切 , 或者說這個可以實現的事實 , 是實體世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們的形式存在於宇宙中其他部份的特殊關係是什麼呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 它是對的 , 但它是錯的 。 有一點是錯的--強調沒有任何特殊的物理特徵 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它的作用 , 很簡單 , 就是我們這裡有三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理的形式是計算 , 計算需要--電腦是無從得知製造電腦的方法 , 而不需要物質 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	接著 , 第三點 , 較不具體 , 但在開放式的創造中 , 知識、解釋的必要性一樣 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境中充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好拿到測試 , 假設牛頓的重力定律是在三百年前提出的 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們平常做的證據 , 在那之前的數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在之後的數十億年繼續墜落.在其他的科學領域也一樣.
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本的真理的證據就在我們的星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	出於星系間空間這三個創造開放式知識的前題條件其可能性最低
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 那裡很冷 , 外面天黑 , 還是原來 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹義的誤解
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像在星系間空間中有個立方體存在 , 跟我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 這個立方體非常的空 , 以人類的標準來看 , 但這仍然意味著 , 它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠建造一個自給自足的太空站 , 上面有一群科學家 , 他們致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 以此類推 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技甚至超越了星系間空間的氫氣將其轉化成其他的元素等等
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某物不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 除了知道如何做 , 還有什麼能阻止我們這麼做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到那我們就會自動獲得能源供應 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片.但是你要做的就是拿個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到同樣的星系.
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	使用更強大的望遠鏡你將可以看到恆星和行星
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 並瞭解物理定律.
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	也許最難做得科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花上億年的時間才能回到最近的有生命得星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但我從來都不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年才進行一次.
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了開放式知識創造的所有前題條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都有可能變成跟我們一樣的中心 , 只要我們知道如何在那邊出現 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們並不是在一個獨特的友好環境下 ,
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式解釋 , 那幾乎其他所有的環境也是 。 地球也是一樣 。 地球也是受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而知識 , 非常匱乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個知識型的宇宙觀也許--而我認為應該要讓我們覺得很特殊.但同時也應該要讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著如果沒有那些必要的具體知識去面對宇宙中存活下來的挑戰 , 我們將無法生存.
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星 , 幾光年外就會爆炸 , 我們都將會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都錯了 , 還有最重要的是使用大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活到這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他之後會在研討會上討論這個議題 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為這個機率是正確的類別可以用來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我確實同意他的看法 。 我們能生存 , 我們不能生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否及時創造了相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險還不是前所未有的物種會絕種
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 。 大部份的物種和所有的文明已然存在 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來說 , 我們唯一的希望是要利用區分我們物種的這個特徵 , 和我們的文明 , 和其他所有其他物種的特殊關係--也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 現在讓我把它用在當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來闡述我所說的這類的話題 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而這個爭議就是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種對的物理學家 。 考慮到全球暖化 , 我只是個懶人 。 理性來說 , 理性的做法是嚴肅看待常見的科學理論 。 而根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 避免災難發生 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果目前我們最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 它限制了經濟活動 , 以及花費數千億美元或其他東西的龐大成本 , 那麼不管用哪種方式 , 這就已經是場災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而倡導的動作甚至都不是為解決問題 , 只是稍微延後一點 。 這樣已經太遲了 , 可能根本就無法避免了 , 在任何人意識到這個危險之前 , 就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 當時最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河期 , 在數十億的年代裡 , 冰河會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它不是在告知公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法一直知道.當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決它的代價就低於災難本身的代價 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防原則 , 可以避免我們還沒有預見到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 而不僅是針對問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒方法但這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被鼻子打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學不是教你如何閃躲拳頭.
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不去尋求治療 , 只專注在預防上 , 那麼它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	當下世界正在忙著用計劃來強行減排不計代價 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該趕快計畫如何降低溫度 , 因計劃生存於更高溫 , 成本也不高 , 但成本要更低 , 又要更便宜 。 有些這類計劃的確存在 , 像空間中一群鏡子偏離陽光 , 並鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒有意識到問題的存在 , 我們能夠運用正確的運氣 , 不是無限期的躲過 , 唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是解決問題 , 而是解決生存的問題 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩塊石板在上面刻上
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 "
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果被困在一個惡劣的制度下 , 國家要如何擺脫貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默開拓出一個大膽的想法: 「 特區市政府 」 , 由一個國家聯盟來統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的根本想法: 「 特區市 」
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	為我們帶來了一個非常引人入勝的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做功課地點是在首都機場的路燈下因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我也見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	讓我們選一個就好比綠色襯衣的好例子 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森擁有手機
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題來了:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以擁有像手機這樣尖端的科技產品卻無法享受老早就有的科技好讓自己家裡有電燈用 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 " 規則 "
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以防止雙贏辦法的產生 , 當人們可以把新技術帶入像尼爾森這樣的人進來 , 可以給他們機會 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循的規則運作就是說 , 它必須以非常低廉的補貼價格來銷售電力事實上 , 這個價格低到它每賣出的單位都一樣
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去連結許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這條規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見過 , 是有可能有不同的規則 , 能讓企業獲利的規則 , 所以他們有動機去幫助更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這種規則就是nelson電信公司的電信購買者從一個底下操作的電話公司 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經知道這些規則如何運作得很好 ,
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試圖改變用電方式定價的規則 , 但卻發生在企業及消費者的抗議活動中 , 他們想保留現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他深陷其中 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森卡在路燈下讀書
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著去找出我們能如何改變規則
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些我們可以發展用來改變規則的規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見讓我們能夠實際地去做 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多選擇 , 更多的領導者更多的選擇 , 在許多國家 , 也都是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現出這兩者之間的反對聲浪很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想給領導者的那種選擇 , 例如:給總統一個選擇 , 以提高電價 , 帶走經濟中人民想要的那種選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給其中一邊或另一邊 , 你就會得到壓力或摩擦 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那會給我們一套制度來改變規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想見識體制的破壞力是如何使人們生活在黑暗中不妨看看美國太空總署拍攝的地球夜景
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果拉近一點來看這裡你可以看到北韓這塊跟鄰國比起來就像是個黑洞
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會驚訝地發現 , 北韓的體制使人留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是要認識到北韓和南韓開始時用的是一模一樣的規則 , 無論是法律或法規 , 都一樣 , 都一樣 , 但在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 導致他們在一組規則中走上非常不同的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變 , 我們人類可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一區:加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	把海地放大 , 這裡的輪廓
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗與它的鄰居多明尼加相比卻有著相同數量的居民
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都是黑暗的相比波多黎各各各只有海地或多明尼加共和國一半的居民
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地提醒我們的是 , 體制之所以不良 , 可能是因為政府的軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	這不僅僅是規則條例不好 , 因為政府太強勢、壓迫 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造一個有良好體制的環境 , 我們不能只是破壞 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法去建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展現出與規則一同工作的潛在和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料的一開始 , 中國是高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人的科技像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等都是先驅
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的制度來鼓勵這些想法的傳播 , 是一種利益的動機 , 可以鼓勵這些想法的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	而且他們很快就會採用一些規則來放慢創新並將中國與世界隔絕
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以當其他國家開始創新不僅發展新科技更建立新制度時中國卻無緣參與這些進步
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	國民所得停滯不前也不再是世界的未來
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 ,
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	顯示中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代時你們可以看到這個數字大約是3%
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況有了變化 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國開始起飛中國人開始急速地追上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你們回想一下 , 晚上在地圖上畫出的線索你就能知道中國制度的大幅變化
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的這點就是你們在輪廓邊上看到的這點是香港
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國領土中很小的一點在20世紀大部分的時候都是遵循一套很不一樣的體制在運作著 , 與中國其他地方的中國規則相比 , 當時中國的市場經濟法則是重複製的 , 由英國主導 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在50年代 , 香港是一個成千上萬人都可以去的地方 , 從主地開始 , 到縫紉上的工作 , 像是上衣、製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但是 , 為了增加收入 , 增加技能 , 在那兒成長得非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本 , 像鄧小平這種領導者可以複製 , 當他們決定把整個大陸通通通向市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以與其強迫所有人立刻轉而支持市場模式不如從設立一些特區著手從某方面來說 , 英國人所做的是讓機會與市場體制一同上手
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建了四個經濟特區讓中國人民可以到這些地方工作 , 城市也很迅速地成長 ; 還有一些外國企業可以進來生產東西的特區 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個特區 , 有一個城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市有台灣企業 , 讓在座很多人都擁有iphone , 而且他們把中國人的勞動力搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿海城市依循相同的概念開張 , 最終 , 在這些地方人民可以選擇成功 , 他們聚集到一起 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	成功的實現了這項共識使整個經濟體向市場模式邁進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了以下幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人民的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模要選對
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試圖改變一個村落的體制 , 你可以這麼做 , 但村落實在太小了以至於你如果有數百萬人在好的體制下工作 , 你就會得到什麼好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家的規模太大了
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試圖改變國家的體制 , 你無法給一些人一個機會 , 去看看事物的結果 , 讓其他人去試著改變規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你這個機會 , 來創造新的地方 , 用新規則 , 讓大家可以選擇要去哪裡 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們就夠大了 , 足以讓我們在幾百萬人一起合作時所能帶來的益處全都在一起 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	因此提議的概念就是我們構思了一個叫做 " 特區市 " 的概念
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個明確規範的憲章開始 , 規定所有規則來吸引建造城市所需的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們會需要吸引投資者這些人將投資興建各項基礎建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場和建築物
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引企業他們會先雇用移居過來的人
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	然後你會需要吸引家家戶戶願意搬來永久居住在那裡養育子女並開始他們的第一份工作
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	這個城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	而我們能把這個模式擴大 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次的
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些被收錄到的憲章裡
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要提供人民選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	那才是真正建構在這個模型上 , 如果我們允許在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從無人居住的領域開始
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以來到新的憲章之下 , 但沒有人被迫在之下生活 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的領導者的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作能夠產生一種潛在的可能性:國家之間可以互相合作 , 事實上 , 中國和英國之間可以互相合作 , 首先是市場模式的一個小小的奴隸 , 接著擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	英國倒是無意間藉由香港的行動減少了世界貧窮比上個世紀所有援助計畫的總和還要多
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這樣的合作模式再度重現我們可以使全世界都受惠
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會牽涉到負責任的地位 , 將控制權下放給一個國家 , 以掌控某些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始會想: 「 這能讓殖民主義復活嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但很重要的是要認清當我們開始思考這些事情時會產生的那種情緒 , 能夠阻擋我們 , 讓我們停止努力 , 讓我們停止努力探索新點子的能力 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這跟殖民主義不一樣 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在一些援助計畫中 , 殘留的就是它涉及了強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式關乎選擇 , 為領導者以及將來居住在這些新地方的人民做出選擇 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	還有 , 選擇就是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們以一個特別的領袖來看 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的事然而古巴並沒有像香港那樣的小島
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他還是有一點點光線在南部 , 那兒有著很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一塊區域 , 在那裡 , 條約為美國的行政負責任一塊大概是曼哈頓的兩倍大的土地 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理對他說: " 嘿 , 美國佬的人有可怕的公關問題
they want to get out .	他們想離開
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你們加拿大何不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	經營一個特殊行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	在那裡建造一座新城市 。
allow many people to come in .	允許許多多人加入
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會遷入那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會想辦法 。 但這將會是把現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模式還可以在哪裡試行呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾與非洲領導人談過 ,
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們當中有許多人完全了解一個特區的想法 , 讓人民可以選定一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	一個可以改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種制定新規則的方式 , 讓人民在不受威脅下可以採取強制手段 , 而對手可以強制執行 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全理解 , 在某些情況下他們可以對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾而這些投資者將會建造港口 , 建造道路 , 在新城市裡 , 他們可以做出更有保障的承諾只要他們能與合夥的國家一起做 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在一些安排有點像信託管理帳戶你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡然後交由合夥的國家管理
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以用來建造新城市
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是一張我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地有數億人可以居住
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們總結一下 , 不只一、二個特區客機 , 還有幾十個城市 , 將來可以為數億人創造居住空間 , 可能是幾十億人 , 在未來的世紀 , 遷移到城市裡有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們晚上去看這些燈光 , 唯一會造成誤導的就是 , 視覺上 , 看起來世界上大部分的地區都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	將這塊土地的代表性
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	這些點代表的是已經被三十億人居住的城市所帶走的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現這些有30億居民的城市只佔了地球上所有可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要再為數十億人建造城市 , 就會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從3%的耕地轉變為4%
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們將大幅減少人類在地球上的足跡 , 通過建造更多人們可以移動到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是依照良好的體制在管理 , 它們可能會是城市 , 讓人們安全地不受犯罪、疾病和衛生不良影響 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電力這樣的基礎設施
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要如何開始建造 「 特區城市 」 , 擴大這個城市的規模 , 來建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	一本手冊會有幫助 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的就是撰寫一些細節 , 可能順利進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理這些城市 , 到外面去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們到野外去 ,
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設不只加拿大和卡斯楚有關的事 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也參一腳 , 西班牙 。 或許古巴想成為四向合作的一員 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有先例可循 , 但很容易解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們該如何資助呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡跟香港是一座非常有價值的城市 , 他們剛起步時 , 所擁有的土地價值因而獲得巨大的成長 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法院等物資的收入 , 但學校和醫療體系也同樣會讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓居民有高所得進而使土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建設這塊區域的人的獎勵 , 並建立這塊區域 , 並建立基本規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其它類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本的建築物 , 且能夠負擔得起第一份工作的人 , 把iphone組裝起來 , 但要讓那些建築物能有效率 , 且要確保它們是安全的 , 不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	有很多技術上的細節尚待處理不過我們這群已經開始追求這些事的人早就知道 , 沒有路上的障礙除了想像力以外沒有其他東西能阻止我們提供真正的全球性的雙贏解決方案
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們能夠這麼幸福儘管地球上人口這麼多都是因為 " 想法 " 的力量
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法 , 他們就和我們分享了 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀有物品 , 分享就意味著我們每個人都會少吃東西 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式來思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法指的是主宰我們彼此的互動規則例如 , 讓我們來訂個賦稅制度來支持一個研究型大學提供一些免費的知識
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有個制度 , 在那裡 , 我們擁有政府辦公室註冊的土地 , 讓大家可以宣誓擔任抵押貸款 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在制度上創新 , 尤其是想出一些規則來改變制度的創新 , 那麼我們就不會卡在不良的制度上 , 那麼我們可以不斷進步 , 真正使這個世界變得更好 , 這樣尼爾森和他的朋友就不再需要在路燈下讀書了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	克萊格•凡特從他史詩般的圓環世界遠征起了一段時間來談談 , 他的團隊目前已經發現了數百萬種基因 , 用來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技企業家、基因學家、發明、科學、科技、科技
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特寫在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對老化議題的意見 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將是我對它的唯一評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	我了解樂觀主義者生活得比悲觀者還要久
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在這18分鐘內我將告訴各位的是我們如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到開始自我編碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前的這個月我們公佈了第一組取自一種非寄生有機體的基因序列像是嗜血桿菌
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月進行的基因研究 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八個小時來完成相同的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年間 , 有大量的基因組被加進來:大部分人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這個想法的基礎上 , 基因組學是在10多年前發生的 , 到今年年底 , 我們可能已經有3到5組基因組的測序 ; 這只是約幾百組的基因序列 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登與貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得贊助 , 到今年將130組基因組定序成為環境有機體的副項目 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	因此讀取基因編碼的速度已經改變 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎不在地球上現有的東西上挖掘地表 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人沒有意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球上生物總量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人常做的事 , 但如果你去到海邊 , 吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約100萬隻細菌和一千萬隻病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	到兩年前 , 只有少於五千種微生物已經被特化 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了二次超棒的海洋考察 , 嘗試採集樣本 , 每200英哩就有一次 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 工作到美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上進行此項任務 , 有部分是要協助讓年輕人興奮地進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗是非常簡單的
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	只要取得海水、過濾 , 再用不同的濾網來蒐集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回在岩城的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以在24小時內完成一億個字母的基因編碼的測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這個活動 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 一般認為在我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩種有機體具有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有生活在海洋上方溫暖地區的物種都有著相同的感光器 , 利用陽光作為牠們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	在一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新的基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在把這個方法延伸到空中 , 加上史隆基金會的贊助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	測量我們每天所呼吸的病毒和細菌的數量 , 尤其是在飛機上 , 或關閉的講堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們利用一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 僅僅一天之內我們在紐約市一棟大樓的樓頂就蒐集到10億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在所在的排序過程中 ,
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在收集資料方面 , 就在加拉帕戈斯的位置 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每隔200英里 , 我們在海洋中可以看到非常多樣的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	這當中有些符合邏輯 , 可以從不同的溫度梯度
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這張是根據溫度拍攝的衛星照片--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色則是冷的--我們發現 , 在溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本上有極大的差異 , 在豐富的物種上 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人訝異的事是這些光感接收器可以偵測到不同波長的光我們也可以根據他們的胺基酸序列來預測這些光
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些因素在各地區產生巨大的變化 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在很深的海洋中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光細胞傾向於看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但變化更大的可能是紅外線和紫外線在極端的光線
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	就為了評估基因庫的樣貌 , 我們把所有的資料整合起來 , 包括所有目前實地考察過的資料 , 它代表地球上所有的基因資料的一半以上 , 總計大約有2千9百萬組基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家庭裡 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果我們發現 , 大約有5萬個主要的基因族群 , 但是我們在環境中採取的每一種新樣本 , 都只能在這些新族群中以線性方式流傳 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於發現基礎基因、元件以及地球上生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的演化樹圖時 , 我們在右上角和動物在同一區 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在這大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組中只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果把所有動物的基因放在一起 , 我們所共有的基因族群大概只有三萬不到一點 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看出這些基因現在不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心論來看-或許回到了理查•達金斯的想法而不是基因組中心論 , 這是這些基因組成分的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 也就是合成dna的能力 , 在過去十到二十年中 , dna定序的速度一直在改變 , 且越來越快 , 越來越便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對於人造基因組的第一個想法來自於1995年我們在第二組基因組的測序 。 這是從mycoplasma生殖支原體中取得的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有非常棒的t恤衫上面寫: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們單純地問一個問題:如果一個物種需要800 , 另外500 , 有更小一組基因組 , 可能組成一個最小的作業系統嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子誘變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子是隨機插入基因編碼的小段的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果置入基因的正中間 , 會阻斷其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有可以接受轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常重要的 , 你只能依據環境中生存的本質或不可或缺的基因來定義 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 和13種相似有機物的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較它們的基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們找到了173種基因 。 所有13種有機體 , 只有173種 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池子如果我們忽略了一個細胞內的寄生蟲 , 會稍微擴大一點點 。 當我們觀察核心組的基因 , 大約是310組左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此我們認為可以藉由你的觀點來擴展或收縮基因組 , 或從最少的500個基因組中 , 延伸到300到400個 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一可以證明這些想法的方法是建造一個包含有這些基因的人染色體 。 我們不得不以一種模塊式的結構來進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現要在大片片片中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 是我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法能讓我們在兩週內製造一種5000個鹼基對的病毒基因序列和生物學上的精準度達到100% 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個令人振奮的實驗我們將合成的dna注入細菌體內 , 突然間dna開始製造病毒粒子反過來殺死細菌
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是人造病毒的首度問世-小兒麻痺病毒一年前成功被製出但只有原病毒1/100的活性且花了3年的時間才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體能打造自身硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻轉而關心生物戰的議題 。 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 也參加了美國政府設立的專門委員會來檢討這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為將現實擺在腦海中是很重要的 , 相對於人們想像的結果 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成測序的病毒基因組都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會馬上對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚慌 , 但是這個生物的dna並沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造出天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會引起感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的是設計師的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有美國和前蘇聯兩國付出極大努力企圖製造生物武器
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這研究真的被終止了 , 那將來在製造設計病毒上就應該不會有太多的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為兩年內就有可能有單細胞生物了 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	那些我們已經擁有的真核細胞 , 可能在十年內就會實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	因此 , 我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變放入這個人造染色體的卡帶和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把所有其他的
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 接著我們有一個同源重組的系統將這些片段組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	这是自一个生物上得到的 , deinoccusradiodurans , 它能承受三百萬拉德的輻射且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後它會在12至24小時內重組自己的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 也許現在可能由於我們在太空中的所有旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過50萬拉德輻射照射過後的杯 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始碎裂 , 而微生物落在底部 , 變得越來越開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的照片上方顯示了經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	其染色體被完全分崩離析 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	而這邊是相同的dna在24小時後自行重組的 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些生物能做到這點真的很讓人吃驚 , 我們在這個星球上有成千上萬種不同的物種有能力做到這點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此我們認為人造細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不單是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 也希望從環境和社會問題中獲得 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上詹氏甲烷鏈球菌:它生存在沸騰的水中其能量來源是氫它所獲得的碳元素則是來自環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	因此我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 都從二氧化碳中生存 , 而能將其捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	因此 , 與其從使用石油中取得碳來進行合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳並將它從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種微生物 , 能靠一氧化碳生存 , 我們用它來降低水分的能量 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數可以改造的甲烷路徑 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦正在和挪威石油公司合作開發一項重大的項目從天然氣田中將甲烷捕獲並轉變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為會有一個新領域出現 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為這些新的合成功能 , 這些巨大的基因陣列和同源重組技術 , 我們想我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造或許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 像所有生物學一樣 , 你能通過篩選來獲得選擇 , 不管你是要檢驗氫氣生成或是化學生成 , 還是可行 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 很快就能了解到 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用的過程直接從陽光產生氫氣
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的氫化酶將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在進行蛋白質的組合 , 將複雜糖分子拆解成簡單糖分子的酶在同一個細胞中進行發酵以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	利用微生物進行製藥生產的實踐早已在各大實驗室中 ,
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物 , 比我們最好的化學家所生產的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來改造的物種可以成為食物的來源 , 希望可以成為能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許可以替換石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這的確是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的教義作為律法 , 卻找不到任何關於禁止製造生命的條件 , 所以這方面就沒問題了 。 最終的卻是生物戰的方面的擔憂 , 卻給我們啟動了這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	史隆基金會為此剛剛資助了一個多機構的研究項目 , 來找出對社會風險和益處的研究結果 , 以及科學團隊們比如我自己的團隊 , 應該在這個領域使用的規則 , 我們試著在未來建立好的榜樣 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義威脅之外 , 它們是簡單的議題 , 就生物學來說 , 我們是否能設計出乾淨的能源 , 或許能徹底改變發展中國家能做的事 , 並提供各種簡單的處理 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普津巴多說 , 快樂和成功都根植在我們之間 , 大部分人忽略的特質:我們對過去、現在 , 及未來的定位 。 他建議我們準時校準自己的觀點 , 成為改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一套健康的手段 , 就如同時間 ,
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些想法 , 關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始計時.30秒
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜.一切就緒.
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	這是關於時間 。 結束排序 。 拿一個吧 。

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來聽聽亞當和校長的誘惑對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當好了 , 不要那麼渴望清洗 。 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我照做了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 咬一口 , 亞當 。 不要拋棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 咬一口 。 搞什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生就是誘惑 。 這一切都是為了產出、抗拒 , 是的 , 沒錯 , 現在 , 晚一點 , 衝動 , 思考 , 關注現在和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	應許之道德會打敗現階段的熱情
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前確保貞操的少女感謝小布施-大多數 , 約有60% , 會在一年內得到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們多數都沒有採取避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	以至於承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們試試四歲的小孩 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但是如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆了 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 就要等了 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的事是 , 三分之二的孩子會在忍受誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等.而其他人 , 當然的 , 要等了.
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲了晚年的到來
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我斯坦福大學的同事 , 在十四年後 , 試圖去發現那些孩子不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 反抗的孩子和產生後代的孩子之間存在著巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	反抗的孩子sat的成績高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很龐大 , 就像是一整組不同的智商點 ,
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信且決心十足 。 而我今天的關鍵 , 對你們來說 , 關鍵在於他們是以未來為中心 , 而不是以現在為中心 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	看待時間是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 如何將你的人類經驗分成不同的時間區域或時間類別.
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動地、無意識地在做這件事 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平都不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	而問題在於它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了過度使用它們 , 反而低於使用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做了一個決定 , 決定是要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 這只與當下情境有關 , 其他人做的事和你的感受有關 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	這些人做決定時 , 會以這種形式作決定 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現實主義 」 。 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在已經不重要了 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去經歷過的這個狀況如何 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定會依據過去的記憶 ,
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 " 懷舊主義 " , 因為他們著重在
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對另一些人 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只是未來而已 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的重點總是在於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱他們為 " 理想主義 " .他們關注的是未來.
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想論 , 時間悖論的觀點 , 是影響你做出的每個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	以這些偏差的角度來看的話
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	實際上 , 這裡有六種 。 有兩種方式可以當下存在 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩個路徑是 「 懷舊主義 」 , 兩種未來的方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	也可以是 " 享受主義 " , 也可以說你專注於享受生活的樂趣 , 或是當權主義者--這無關緊要的 , 你的生活受到控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 " 理想主義 " , 設定目標
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	開發思維的靈活性 , 轉換時間的觀點 , 會流暢地依據局面的需求 , 這是你得學會的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光資料 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度 " 未來
and moderate on presenthedonism .	及現代主義的準則 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠放低 " 負面懷舊 " 及 " 宿命論 "
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最佳時光透視的混合是來自過去的積極樂觀帶給你的根源 。 你連結家人、身份和自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來是一對翅膀 , 可以飛到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
