what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	享樂主義是能量 , 探索自身所在地、人與人之間的能量 ,
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光審視就會有比正面更高的負面情緒 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲什麼呢 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間 ; 犧牲朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 ; 犧牲個人嗜好 ;
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠.所以這會影響他們的健康.
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們的生活是為了工作 , 成就和控制 ,
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 對一些ted會員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這讓我產生共鳴 。 我成長過程中是個貧窮的孩子 , 住在南布朗克斯貧民窟 , 西西里島的家庭 , 每個人都過去和現在都生活在過去 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡 , 作為一個未來的主管 , 走到頂端 , 做出這些犧牲因為老師介入了 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為只要等就可吃到兩顆了 , 直到我學會保持平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上現今的說法 , 把焦點放在正面 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說我們把這種方法用在世界各地的問題上:改變輟學率、增加毒癮、增加青少年健康、用時間隱喻法治療退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 促進永續發展和保育 , 減少身體康復費用 , 此項目有50%的退出率 , 改變自殺式恐怖主義的訴求 , 並改變家庭關係 , 修正學生的衝突 , 修正家庭關係 , 修正學生的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想在結尾做結:生活中許多難題可以被解答 , 只要了解你的時間觀點和他人 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	想法是如此簡單、明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	當今的新聞頭條中有多少人會在100年後重要 ? 1000年 ? 克克洛克克克克克•卡特朗的《長期新聞》收集不只重要的報導數十年後 , 甚至會在數十年後引起共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調出頭條可能會形塑我們未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題 , 媒體 , 新聞 , 科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事會有多少在長期來看是很重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是由tedsters所創立的 「 長遠的基金會 」 計畫其中包括kevinkelly和stewartbrand
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們在尋找的是一個可能在50或100或100 , 000年後仍然會有重要的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你通過過濾器看新聞 , 很多東西會掉在旁邊 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 採用a.p.的首要故事 , 在十年內 , 這有影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會是重要的嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟問題 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這次經濟衰退新聞就會變成陳年往事 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 怎樣的故事才能為未來帶來改變呢 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就科學而言
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小飛行器會經過我們的血液中進行修復 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 那某一天已經在你身邊了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近發生的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液攻擊腫瘤 ; 他們把基因送到大腦 ; 他們打造的一個可以在人體上爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在連填飽60億人的肚子都有困難 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天所聽到的 , 這裡有超過10億人處於飢餓中 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	沒有基因改造作物 , 英國人會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茲投入了十億美元在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會大不相同 , 如果讓中國來設定議程的話 , 而且他們有可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經推翻美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始在兒童身上做dna測試 , 來選擇職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種途徑 , 來追溯我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	近期有一些新發現:有一個來自阿根廷的蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每一個大陸上 , 但是南極洲 。 有一群自導的機器人科學家 , 他們很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能再也不需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎有沒有人類 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我的決定是去年的長遠新聞主題是這一個:在月球上發現了水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓殖民地更容易放到上面 ,
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果nasa沒有做到 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某位也可能會寫下大筆支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅琳•波爾科所展示的圖片從卡西尼航行到土星 , 將目光集中在它最大的衛星 「 泰坦 」 上 , 以及冷凍的土衛二上 , 它似乎對冰噴射機造成衝擊 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛往土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶大家去旅行 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段旅程 , 你和我已經經歷了很多年 , 50年前 , 當人類第一次離開地球時 , 這段旅程便開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅將物體放到月球上 , 我們還把飛行器給了所有這8顆行星 , 我們讓它落在了這顆小行星上 , 與彗星相遇 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一架太空飛船正向冥王星 , 飛向這顆曾經被我們稱為星球的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械裝置的使命都屬於更大人類旅程的一部分:一趟瞭解某些事物的旅程 , 來感受我們的宇宙之地 , 了解我們的來源 , 了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的星球 , 以及我們賴以生存的地球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在所有我們去探索太陽系的地點中有土星 。 我們去過的地方有土星 。 在1980年代初期我們去過土星之前 , 我們對土星的研究比當時更加深入 , 從卡西尼號太空飛船開始 , 經過了七年星際空間 , 飛越土星的軌道 , 在2004年夏天 , 形成了當時人類史上最遠的太空飛行器 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是一個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它賦予神秘的、科學的洞察力、顯然的輝煌成就 , 而這個系統的研究涵蓋了巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能學到很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 。 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張仙女星雲的照片 , 非常漂亮 , 這是我們最接近、最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這是旋風式銀河系的優美組合 , 由哈勃太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 返回土星的這段旅程 , 其實也是用來做為人類更大探索之旅的一部分 , 用來了解我們周遭所有事物之間的相互關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這幅圖中 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦的是 , 我無法用卡西尼號來告訴各位我們所學的全部 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半拍攝的所有漂亮照片 , 因為我真的沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	下面我將要聚焦在兩件最振奮人心的故事中 , 是我們在土星探險附近進行的兩次探險 , 在過去的兩年半中 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	陪伴在土星周圍的是一系列巨大又多樣的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里寬到跟美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝到的這些土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 呈現出土星與它的衛星在一起 。 這是土星和土衛二有土衛二 , 這是土星的光環 , 這邊有邊是邊緣的邊緣 , 邊緣有多薄 。 藉由月球的土衛二有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星47顆衛星中有兩顆特別耀眼 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二恩克拉多斯 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的 , 未經勘探的單獨地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	而且它是一種長久以來都很好奇的身體 , 看著這些行星的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為更像我們在地球上的環境 , 至少在過去 , 在太陽系中的其他天體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中含有大量氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣被簡單的有機物質淹沒了 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六大氣中被分解出來 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造出霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物無所不在 , 完全被全球化的土衛六覆蓋 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你無法用肉眼看到表面 , 看到我們的眼睛位於光譜的視覺區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但在卡西尼號到達之前 , 我們推測 , 這些霧狀顆粒經過了數十億年的時間 , 慢慢地飄向水面 , 覆蓋著厚的有機泥狀物 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以就像泰坦的焦油 , 油 , 或什麼我們不知道 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們推測的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在泰坦的地表溫度下可以是液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷在土衛六上呈現了水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是會冷凝的 , 所以 , 認知到這種情況 , 整個世界的怪異可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在那些雲之上 , 你能看到幾百公里的霧狀 , 可以防止陽光照射到地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度大約是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管溫度很低 , 土衛六上還是會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上做──地球上雨的功能:它開水溝 ; 它形成河流和白內障 ; 它可以形成峽谷 ; 它可以在大盆地和坑中儲水 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它能把泥狀物從高山上沖下來 , 進入低地 , 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的地表是怎樣的 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡一片漆黑 。 泰坦的中午和地球上的高亮度一樣黑 , 在地球上一片漆黑 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 很陰森 , 很模糊 , 有可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在上面塗料稀釋劑的密西根湖邊 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	在卡西尼號到達卡西尼號之前 , 我們對泰坦星表面的看法是這樣的 , 我可以告訴你 , 我們在泰坦上發現的 , 雖然它和那個故事不太一樣 , 但它卻是那麼吸引人的 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像卡西尼號的人一樣 , 過去就像是朱爾凡爾納的冒險經歷成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	就像我說的 , 它有很厚的層大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 背光的是太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	而那裡還有另一顆衛星--我甚至不知道是哪一顆 。 這是個擴散得很大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有專門儀器 , 透過這個大氣層可以看見水面 , 我的攝影系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍攝了像這樣的照片
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮跟深色的區域 , 那大約是目前為止的狀況 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太神秘了:我們無法知道我們在土衛六上看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你看得更近這一區 , 你會開始看到無數的通道--我們不知道是甚麼 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 這實際上是一個隕石坑 , 但是 , 土衛六表面的隕石坑數量很少 , 意即 , 這是個非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有一些特徵看起來像地殼構造 ,
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來像是被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上的任何線性 , 代表有一個斷層 , 像個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以經過地質構造的改變
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但是我們還是沒辦法理解我們的圖像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月之後 , 一件事情發生了 , 許多人認為是卡西尼號在土衛六上的突出調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 。 歐洲建造的惠更斯號探測器穿越了太陽系七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這是多麼重要的一件事 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製作的儀器 , 它在外太陽系的天體上首次登陸 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心目中 , 這件事意義重大 , 以至於在美國和歐洲都市各處 , 都應承擔起 「 滴答滴答 」 遊行 。 很遺憾 , 事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這對另一個原因意義重大 。 這是國際使命運動會在歐洲、德國還有慶祝活動目的地都是用英語口音來舉辦 , 還有美國口音 , 還有德國口音 , 法語 , 和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個關於 「 聯合國 」 一詞的動態示範應該是要表達的:真正的國家會聯合起來 , 一起努力做出好事 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	為了要探索一顆星球 , 這是個很大的任務 , 為了要了解一個星球系統 , 這個系統在人類歷史上是不可預測的 , 現在人類真的去接觸了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	這真是--我只是說一下 , 就起雞皮疙瘩了 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一個極度情緒化的事件這是我個人永遠無法忘記的事情而且你也不應該這樣做
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在下降的途中對大氣進行了測量 , 它也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法用言語形容第一次看到土衛六地表照片的感覺 。 這是我們所看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這讓人震驚 , 因為這是我們希望其他從軌道上拍的照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	當時的地質模式是很明確的 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是僅靠液體流動才能形成的樹突狀排水模式 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些溝渠找到它們的匯合處 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這條通道中 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這還是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里的高空拍攝
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里高的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--大概就是飛機的飛行高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	若你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在土衛六航空公司的窗口上所看到的照片 , 當你飛越土衛六時 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器停留在地表上 , 我要給各位看 , 各位先生女士 , 這是在外太陽系的衛星表面上拍攝的第一張照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些很可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對吧 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯 , 它落在了其中一塊平坦的陰影地帶 。 它沒有沉沒消失 。 所以它不是我們降落在黑暗的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器下降的就相當於一灘泥漿 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個結合了液態甲烷的大地 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	大概是這樣一來這材料是透過我們看到的這些溝渠沖洗掉土衛六的高地 , 流過數十億年來填充為低窪地帶 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們仍然沒有任何跡象在我們的影像中 , 或者是在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體中都沒有 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們看到沙丘時 , 更令人費解了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們電影中關於土衛六赤道地帶的電影 , 展示了這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 被幾個公里半公里的沙丘 , 它們可以走上好幾英哩 , 甚至好幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有幾百英里 , 高達1000到1200英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然地 , 這裡非常乾燥 , 否則不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	又一次地 , 令人困惑的是沒有任何液體 , 直到我們終於看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	這是土衛六南極的一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現了相當於加勒比海大小的一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 基於某些原因 , 我們不了解液體 , 或至少這個季節 , 很顯然就是在土衛六的極地帶 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個不可思議又神秘的地方 。 它是外星人的 。 但又和地球有著奇怪的相似處 , 而且有著像地球表面一樣的地質構造和極大的地質多樣性 。 它是一個迷人的世界 , 太陽系中 , 複雜度和豐富度只有地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們來看看恩克拉多斯 。 土衛二是小型衛星 , 大小約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以在這邊看到 , 只是為了向你們展示它的尺寸 。 這並不是指威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二很白很亮 , 表面有很明顯的裂痕 ,
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的發現大多集中在南極點上 , 我們看到了南極在這裡 , 我們發現了這個裂痕系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同是因為它們的組成不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被包裹著 。 這些裂縫被有機物質包裹著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地區還提升了溫度 。 這裡是整個星球溫度最高的地方 , 體內最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 因為發現地球上的南極洲比熱帶地區還熱 ,
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 我們拍攝了額外的照片 , 我們發現從這些地裂中 , 有細小的冰粒噴射出來 , 噴射範圍為方圓幾百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	而當我們對這個圖片進行顏色分析 , 將微弱的光源抽出 , 我們看到這些噴射流在土衛二上方幾千英里的地方 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊檢查了像這樣的圖片 , 就像這張圖 , 思考了卡西尼號帶來的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們已經得出結論 , 這些噴射現象可能從土衛二地表下的液態水噴發而出 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過剩的熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其他生命的發現 , 無論是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學的意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明在我們的太陽系中 , 創世紀已經發生過不止一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立於兩次 , 那就表示 , 透過推斷 , 它在宇宙中發生過無數次 , 且在137億年的歷史上 , 都是如此 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆有生命存在的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是那麼珍貴 , 獨一無二 。 它依然是我們唯一的家園 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座的哪位1960年代的時候頭腦還靈活--請原諒你們 , 如果你們不了解 , 沒關係的話 , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人拍下的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是地球第一次從太空拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中的地位產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對於保護地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們的卡西尼號同樣拍下了一張人類眼睛前所未見的圖 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是在日全蝕的時候 , 從土星的另一端看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無與倫比的照片中 , 看到背著太陽的主環 , 看到太陽折射後的形象 , 還看到由土衛二的噴氣輪產生的光環 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這些都還不夠聰明 , 我們還可以在這美麗的圖像中找到我們自己的星球 , 依著土星光環的臂彎堆起來 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 關於從遠處觀看我們自己有著深入的感動 , 並捕捉到我們天空中小小的、藍色的行星 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 以及我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能就是 , 最終 , 是我們獲得的最佳獎賞 , 也是半個世紀前開始的發現 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年為止 , 只剩下15%的世界標註地圖 。 這張圖減緩了災難後援助的程序 , 隱藏了未被使用之地與未知之路的經濟潛力 。 在這個短短的演講中 , 谷歌的katragadademos地圖 , 全球各地的人用繪製的團體繪製工具 , 繪製了他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的katragada:為對抗災難的製作地圖 , 建構經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 塞隆納基斯摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需救助
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要運送人員物資進城 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有標示道路的地圖也沒有醫院的地圖也沒有可以幫助到氣旋受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區對應到可數位化的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國跟世界大部分的人口面臨的問題沒有詳細的地圖
but help was coming .	但救兵來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google有40位志願者使用了新軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 運輸和救護站
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個鼓勵我們每個人在當地標註地圖的科技 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們使用這套軟體標註了道路、河流、學校、當地企業錄影帶出租店 , 到轉角的便利商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎被提名人hermandodesoto認爲開發中國家要發展經濟最重要的關鍵是去掌握大量未清查的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度就有價值一兆美元的土地沒被列入考量 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年170個國家數以千計的使用者就標註了幾百萬筆資訊並創造了一份細節的地圖這份地圖從來不覺得可行
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這是因為各地熱情的使用者的力量所實現的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們現在來看看使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	話說回來 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們在繪製170個國家的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的bridget剛為塞內加爾標註了一條道路
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離這裡近一點 , chalua , 班加羅爾的ng.路上
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是融合了計算機幾何學動作識別和機器學習的結果
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是幾百個城市裡數千個使用者的勝利一個使用者一次編輯一筆資訊
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這也是對70%未被涵蓋的星球的一個邀請
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦的巴勒斯坦村落動了十個月長的非暴力抗爭 , 阻止一個在橄欖園上的障礙 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 巴西的巴勒斯坦的製片人尤利亞•巴查亞問:為什麼我們只注意以色列抗爭中的暴力 , 而不是針對有一天可能帶來和平的非暴力領袖 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱麗亞•巴夏:注意非暴力衝突 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品他們試圖用和平手段來結束衝突
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我與歐洲及美國旅行時 , 總會有一個問題:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 經常我才從中東回國 , 我在那裡拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人運用非暴力方法來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 這些人來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人致力於推動一場大規模的全國非暴力運動來結束這場佔領並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但大多數人可能從未聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂 , 介於發生在地面上的狀況 , 以及對國外的事情的看法之間的分歧 , 是我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功的關鍵原因 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要來談關注的力量你的關注的力量以及非暴力運動在約旦河西岸、加薩及其他地方的新興和發展而今天 , 我的個案研究是巴勒斯坦
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力持續成長的主要原因 , 並不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要讓我們開始注意那些已經擁有非暴力手段的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	請允許我藉由把你們帶到這個名為布德鲁斯村的村落來闡述這個論點
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前他們面臨了滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈要建起分離的障礙 , 一部分的障礙會建在村落的上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並且被包圍住如此便無法自由往返約旦河西岸的其他地方
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領袖的鼓舞 , 他們發動了和平反抗運動 , 阻止了這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以瞭解到實際在地表上的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會分隔巴勒斯坦和以色列
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村我們發現這道牆將竊取我們的土地
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男性:這柵欄事實上創造了解決恐怖問題的方案
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你的身邊是數十位你的以色列弟兄姐妹
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:軍隊害怕的就是非暴力反對者 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女性:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們都不能那麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女生們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空腦中的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要把它傳播到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號聲:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯、受歡迎的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍籬的衝突持續著
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來驅散群眾
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是實彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就好像普魯杰 。 四處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我之前確定我們一定會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但我身邊還有一些人甚至一點都不害怕 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭是無法阻止其發展的 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱麗亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一不平凡的事件而那就是七年前 , 2003年發生的事件
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的以色列與巴勒斯坦的領土分界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍全約旦河西岸的村子以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦人居住的地區
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體還是沒有報導這些故事
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種漠視嚴重的影響非暴力運動在巴勒斯坦發展甚至存活的可能性
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點它們都是劇院的一種形式--尋求他們的理想
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有使用暴力的人才能上頭版並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題非暴力領袖就很難向他們的社區證明公民抗命是個可行的選擇來解決困境
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能對在場的父母親一點都不驚訝
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子丟出越來越大聲的嬰兒的方式 , 就是第一次給他注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	這種吵鬧的行為將成為兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為因為孩子知道他能從中得到父母的注意力
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予孩童注意力或是不給予孩童注意力來鼓勵或抑制這樣的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區及國家的行為都可能受到影響 , 端看國際社會選擇聚焦在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信在結束中東地區的衝突的核心處 , 將和平帶入非暴力行為 , 將非暴力行為轉變成為功能性行為 , 做法是讓更多的注意到當代的非暴力領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝約旦河西岸的村子加薩地區以及東耶路撒冷的村子時 , 我見證到就算只是一部紀錄片也能影響整個轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	瓦拉杰村座落的位置非常接近耶路撒冷那裡的人面臨跟布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將被包圍並失去許多土地也將失去往返約旦河西岸或耶路撒冷的自由
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力運動兩年了 , 但因為沒有人注意到他們 , 卻漸漸被放棄 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩選方式 ,
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後他們舉辦了至今最完善、有紀律的展示
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	舉辦人說村民見到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在一部影片後覺得確實有人在跟隨他們的所作所為人們是在乎的
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續往前 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列那邊則有名為索里德拉爾特的和平運動在希伯來語中代表團結一致
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這些運動的領袖都把布德鲁斯村當做主要的徵召工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們回報說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 在看電影的時候 , 可以了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰村和索里德拉爾特的運動展現出即使是小型預算的獨立製片也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力行為轉化為功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者能夠擁有的權力 , 假如他們開始報導這些村落中發生的非暴力抗爭 , 像是bil、ni'in、瓦拉杰 , 所在的耶路撒冷地區 , 如謝赫賈拉和silwan , 非暴力領袖在他們的作品中會變得更加明顯、有價值、有效果 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要理解 , 如果我們不關注這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像它們從未發生一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見過 , 如果我們親身經歷了 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們能成長 , 它們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中生長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力就是那種終於可以解開局面的影響力
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的就算在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們關注他們 , 讓他們能夠證明到處都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•薩克有一個簡單但強大的領導模式 , 都是從一個金色圈和 「 為什麼 」 開始的 。 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金、和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導能力 , 銷售業務 , 成功銷售
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•薩克:偉大領袖如何激勵大家行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所想的一般時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠完成似乎違反所有假設的事情時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	比如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們的創新能力甚至超過了所有的競爭對手 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們也對有同樣才華的人有相同的管道接觸同樣的廣告商、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德金恩領導黑人民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到平等公民權不公平待遇的人他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能想出如何控制飛行器 ? 為什麼有其他團隊更有資格、更有資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達到發動機飛行的效果 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	而這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法而它甚至深深改變了我如何深深地運作的方式
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大且具有啟發性的領袖和組織──不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩或華特兄弟──他們都以同樣的方式思考、行動與溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且跟其他人完全相反
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是解讀它而它可能是世界上最簡單的想法
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領導人能夠激勵其他人沒有的機構 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這些詞彙 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個人、每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百肯定 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼辦到的 , 不論你怎麼稱呼它是你不同的價值主張 , 或是你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少很少人或組織知道他們為什麼做他們的工作 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 不是指 「 為了獲利 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這就是結果 , 它永遠都是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的起因是什麼 ? 你的信仰是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果是 , 我們的思考方式 , 我們的行為和溝通方式都是由外而內的
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚到最模糊不清的
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受到啟發的領導者和那些受啟發的機構不管它們的規模 , 不管它們的產業都以由內而外的方式去思考、行動與溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果電腦是因為它很容易懂 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦像其他人一樣 , 從他們身上得到的推銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們都設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 使用者也很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」 「 meh 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是多數人溝通的方式
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方法 , 多數業務都是這樣做的這是多數人與人之間的溝通方式
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何比較好並且我們期待某種行為、購買行為、投票行為或這類的事
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶服務
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車它有很好的油耗里程序它有皮革製的座椅 , 買我們的車
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡有蘋果電腦實際上溝通的方式:
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的每件事 , 我們相信都在挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的角度思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很美 , 很簡單 , 用起來也很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉了資訊的順序
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明了人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每一個人都對買蘋果電腦感到相當自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常安心 , 要從蘋果買一台mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但是 , 正如我之前說過的 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	在結構上 , 沒有什麼能區別它們與其競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都有同樣能力製造出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯夠資格製造平面電視
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面螢幕監視器好幾年了
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦推出mp3播放器和pda.他們的產品都有很好的品質而且他們能完美地製造精良設計的產品而且沒有人買
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會向電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是與每個需要你有什麼的人在做生意
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要與那些相信你所相信的人做生意
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	以下是最棒的部分:我告訴各位的都不是我個人的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都以生物學的教條為基礎
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 是生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你去看人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看你看到的是人腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 與黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們人類的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 與 「 什麼 」 的層次對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法以及語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份組成了我們邊緣的腦而我們邊緣的腦是負責所有的感情如信任與忠誠
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也同時負責所有人類的行為所有的決策而它沒有語言的能力
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通時是的 , 人們可以理解龐大數量的複雜資訊像是特色、好處、事實與數字
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是不能推動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能由內而外溝通時 , 我們就在對話中 , 說話的對象是大腦控制行為的部分 , 接著 , 我們允許人們去合理化它 , 用我們說和做有形的事情來做 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是我們用膽識做決定的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給一個人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是什麼 , 但就是感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為管控決策的腦並不控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	而我們最多能整理出的是: 「 我不知道 , 只是感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你說你用心領導 , 或你用靈魂領導著 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想對你說 , 那些都不是身體其他部份在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	所有的發生都在你邊緣的腦裡 , 控制決策而非語言的部份 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼做你正在做的事 , 而人們對為什麼你正在做的事有反應 , 那你怎麼會讓別人為你選票 , 或購買你的東西 , 或更重要的 , 忠實並且想要成為你正在做的事的一份子 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你人生的人 ; 目標是要賣東西給那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不是只在雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道的 , 如果你雇用人僅是因為他們可以做一份工作他們會為了你的錢而工作 , 但是如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人他們會為你工作他們會用血汗與淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	而沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子了
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀初追尋人類飛翔就像今天的網路公司一樣
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功的關鍵在於
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 你為什麼你的產品 , 為什麼你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	而人們總會給你相同的這三件事:不合適、不對的人 , 和不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是這相同的三件事 , 所以我們來探討一下
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley獲得了5萬美金的戰局給了這個飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢是沒問題的 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛任職於smithsonian工作他非常瞭解當時的所有大頭腦
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的人才資金來源也能找到市場情況真是棒極了
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑而且每個人都為langley加油
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們怎麼會從沒聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和維爾伯萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店的現金來支付他們的夢想 ; 沒有任何一位在萊特兄弟的團隊受過大學教育 , 甚至沒有歐維爾或威爾伯等大學 , 紐約時報也無家可歸 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 奧維爾和威爾伯是因一個目標而驅使的 , 靠一個信念驅使的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器這將改變世界的軌道
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 而且他想成名
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人的時候
and lo and behold , look what happened .	然後看 , 發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗與淚水和他們一同努力工作的人
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外那些人則只是為了錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是關於萊特兄弟每次出門前要用五套零件因為這是他們可能墜機的次數在他們出門做供應之前
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛而在場甚至沒有人可以體驗
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley因為錯誤的動機在萊特兄弟起飛那天 , 離職了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我也會在你們的科技上不斷進步 。 」 但他並沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 沒有變有錢他沒有變有名 , 所以他辭職了
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你相信的事物你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂創意的散播法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對知道它的術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5% , 是創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是我們早期使用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數晚期的大多數以及落後者
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式電話的唯一原因是因為你不再買社交電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	在這個尺度上我們都坐在不同的位置 , 不同的時間上但創意的散播法則告訴我們如果你想要在大眾市場成功或者讓大眾市場接受一個想法你不能擁有它直到你到達了在15%到18%之間的市場占有率的引爆點然後系統就會一面倒到你
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 在新事業上你們的轉換率是多少 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意告訴你們: 「 喔 , 值得驕傲的是大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以有超過10%的顧客被絆倒
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大概10%的 「 了解 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是有本能的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是了解 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 先找到那些拿到和他們做生意的人 , 而不是那些拿不到的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	就是這個 , 這個小小的差距 , 你必須要結束 , 就像傑弗瑞•摩爾稱它為的 , 「 跨越鴻溝 」 因為 , 你看 , 早期的多數人不會嘗試直到其他人已經先嘗試為止
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 這些發明家以及早期的採用者他們對做這些需要膽試的決定感到很自在
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更為自在也就是被他們對世界的看法所驅使而不只是產品可以取得
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六個小時買剛上市的iphone的人而當你下個禮拜你剛剛可以走進店裡從架上買下一個
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花40 , 000美金在平面電視上的人當他們剛上市的時候即使這項科技是次等的
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們這麼做並不因為這項科技有多好他們這麼做是為了他們自己
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想當第一
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅證明了你相信什麼
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的原因在最初的六個小時排隊排了六個小時是因為他們所相信的世界以及他們想要每個人如何看他們他們是第一
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	作為商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說 , 成功的訣竅是金錢 , 和適當的人 , 及適當的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	當tivo上市時 , 約8 , 9年前至今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下也是 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們有很高的資金
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的狀況好得不得了
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當成動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是tivo東西在我超時華納的dvr上
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但是tivo卻失敗了
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	而當他們上ipos的時候他們的股票大約是30到40美金然後股價下跌 , 從來沒有在10以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我並不認為這甚至超出6美元 , 除了幾次小漲幅 ,
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有個產品能暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 重溫現場的電視節目 , 且不用問而記住你的收視習慣 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活的、想為你量身打造產品的人 , 我們會為你量身打造產品嗎 ?
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場節目 , 跳過商業廣告記下你的收視習慣等等
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子有關創意的散播法則
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天25萬人在華盛頓的商場上現身聽取金恩博士的演講
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函而當時也沒有網站去查看日期
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是在美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到迫害的人在美國公民權普及前的時代
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的想法有一些很糟
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要被改變
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的人們採取了他的理想 , 將之化為己出 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	而這些人之中的某些人創造了結構 , 讓這個字傳達給更多的人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	各位 , 25萬人在對的時間出現在對的日子 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己出席
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	是他們所相信的美國使他們踏上八個小時車程的旅行在八月中時站在華盛頓的陽光下
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 這不是關於黑人與白人25%的觀眾是白人
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種不同的法律:那些由更高權威以及那些由人類制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	一直到所有法律都由人所定與較高權威制定的法律一致時我們才會生活在一個公平的世界
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動是幫助他終身的完美因素 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物說 , 用他們全面性的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導人持有權力或權威的位置 , 但是那些領導的人啟發了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	無論是個人或組織我們跟隨那些領導的人不是因為我們必須而是因為我們想要
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	而正是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開頭的人 , 能夠啟發他們周遭的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記住你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你如何知道你是正確的方向 ? 神經科學家尼爾伯茲研究我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 以及這些機制如何與記憶、想像力相連 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們把車停在一個很大的停車場 , 我們怎麼記住我們停的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬所面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從黃色標記的海馬體談起 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受到傷害 , 像在阿茲海默症 , 你記不住事情 , 包括你把車子停哪 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文中的 「 海馬 」 , 它的名字是 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	如同大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元所構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內大約有一千億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元間藉由互相連結的小脈衝或突波發送電脈衝 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成它們非常緊密的相互連結
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶的運作方式 , 是記錄老鼠或老鼠在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物時的個別神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們要想像我們記錄一個單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體裡面
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一點電的突波 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到的是 , 這個神經元知道老鼠什麼時候到環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	並藉由電的突波來傳遞訊號給大腦
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	這樣我們就可以把神經元的傳送速度當作是動物在地點的一個功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄很多不同的神經我們可以發現到當動物移動到其環境不同的部位就會有不同的神經發射出訊號像是在這個方形的盒子裡
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們會為其餘的大腦建立一張地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞在人類身上也被記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時候需要腦部監控的電活動
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在一個小鎮裡面開車閒晃
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	河馬體內的位置細胞就會發射 , 活躍起來 , 每當他們開車經過那個城鎮的一個特定位置時 , 就會開始發送電子脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠和老鼠在環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	圖中這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界特別重要
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上面那張圖顯示著老鼠在兩面牆之間的移動發出訊號
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你擴大盒子的位置 , 激發的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面那一層會開火 , 只要南邊有一面牆 ,
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子中放置另一道牆那細胞在這兩個地方都會被激活當動物隨意在箱子裡頭探索時 , 細胞就會被激發出來
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測了感應邊界的距離和方向──延伸建築物的距離等等──這對海馬體是非常重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在輸入海馬體的細胞輸入時 , 海馬體內的細胞就會被發現 , 海馬體的確會根據周遭老鼠或老鼠的遠距離而有反應 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以 , 左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆 , 或是在東邊的界線 , 不論是方形的邊緣或是圓形的方框 , 或圓形的牆壁 , 或甚至是桌邊的邊緣 , 那些動物在那邊跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	細胞當南方有界線的時候就會被激發不管是邊緣還是邊緣的還是牆壁 , 或甚至是兩張桌子間的縫隙
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物在哪裡活動
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以檢驗我們認為物體的位置 , 例如這一目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或是車子的位置 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把牠們放回環境中 , 一般來說牠們不太會把標記移到牠們認為那邊是旗子或是車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以了解到他們認為旗幟位置的改變 , 如何隨著環境的形狀和大小改變而有所改變 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	你可以看到 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗幟位在方形環境的位置 , 然後如果你問問人們那裡的位置 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為國旗的位置和位置細胞被激發的時間完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你記得旗幟的位置藉由在位置細胞的 「 激發模式 」 來儲存你所在位置的所有位置細胞然後你就可以藉著四處移動回到那個位置這樣你就最好符合目前位置細胞被激發的模式與目前儲存模式相吻合
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道透過運動 , 我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們走一些我們可能停車場的路徑 , 並且脫身 , 我們知道因為我們自己的動作 , 可以整合起來這條路徑 , 大致上要往回的方向走 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞亦可得到類似 「 網格細胞 」 的路徑整合 ,
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞也是在海馬體的輸入上找到它有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	當老鼠四處探索的時候每個細胞會激發一系列不同的位置在環境中以驚人的規律三角形網格傳遞
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄數組網格細胞並以不同的顏色標記它們會對環境產生網格激發模式而每個細胞的網格激發模式會稍微跟其他細胞相比
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以紅色的會在這個網格被激發綠色的在這個 , 藍色的在這個
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 就好像這隻老鼠可以在自己的環境內放入一個虛擬空間的網格有點像地圖上所看到的緯度和經度的線條但用的是三角形的網格
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動的時候 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的所在位置 , 讓它可以使用自己的動作 , 來知道它在它的環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有網格激發的模式有著相同的對稱軸線 , 相同的激發方向 , 在這裡用橘色標出的部份 , 這代表在網格細胞的特定部位 , 應該有所改變 , 根據我們是否沿著這六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以將人們放進mri掃描儀 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛剛給你們看的那個 , 然後尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人腦內也看得到腦迴 , 就像你在老鼠身上看到的網格細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得車子的位置和方向以延長建築物和邊界到他停車的地方
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這可以用邊界偵測細胞來表示 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	同時藉由網格細胞激發模式來回憶起他走出車子停車場的道路這些道路將被呈現在電網中
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以使位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	讓他可以藉由移動找到他當初車子停放的位置 , 來找到目前位置與腦中車子停放的地方 , 位置細胞的激發模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個視覺提示的位置 , 比如他的車是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能它已經到達了
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道當初的處境 , 所以他知道去拿
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種網格狀的激發模式 , 我們在一系列的位置上 , 總是處於活躍的狀態 , 當我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記住你上次參加婚禮的那幾次 ,
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 神經運作機制 , 呈現在我們周遭的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這麼一來 , 我們就能重建出空間場景 , 起碼 , 那些曾經發生在我們腦海中的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	如果這正在發生 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始互相啟動 , 通過這些高密度的相互連結 , 然後再重新活化邊界細胞 , 創造出你視野周圍的空間構造 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以在空間中移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種是頭向細胞 , 我還沒提過 , 它們就像是指南針一樣可以根據面向不同的方向而有反應 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從這裡定義你的視覺圖像來定義你的方向 , 讓你可以想像當你在這個婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是認知神經科學裡一個新時代的一個例子我們開始去了解心理的過程像是你怎麼去記憶、怎麼去想像、甚至是怎麼去思考那些構成我們大腦的數十億個神經元活動
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全是由機構、政府、私營部門 , 及公共部門所驅動的合作 。 那不僅僅是對開放風扇的遠景 , 也是在北約熱內托的最高統治者 , 來自近期的軍事歷史中 , 能夠分享時時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全 , 應該要用橋樑而不是靠牆壁來建造 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題開源、和平、政治、社群媒體暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯斯斯特利迪斯:北約的最高統治者如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談一些開放資源的安全性問題 , 因為我們必須在21世紀做得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說說 , 我們回顧二十世紀吧 , 來了解安全這個風格對我們有多大用處 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北方 。
